_Generated 2026-06-05. Findings-only; nothing has been changed. Each finding was produced by a deep-read auditor and independently re-checked by an adversarial verifier; **refuted** findings have been dropped (1 removed)._

## Coverage

- **Dimensions with findings:** 33 / 33.
- **Verified findings (post-refute, deduped):** 194 — **P0 4 · P1 19 · P2 69 · P3 102**.
- **Verdict mix:** confirmed 132, uncertain 1, unverified 61.
- **Still unverified (no verdict file):** `a11y`, `collections`, `i18n`, `journey-media-pdf`, `journey-new-user`, `mobile`, `pdf`, `security`, `settings`, `todo`.
- **104** bugs/correctness/security/data-loss · **90** design/UX/a11y/i18n/perf.

Severity: **P0** = data loss / security / core flow broken · **P1** = major · **P2** = moderate or edge-case · **P3** = minor / polish. Verdict: **confirmed** = verifier re-read the code and agrees · **uncertain** = plausible, needs a runtime check · **unverified** = no adversarial pass yet.

# Part A — Bugs, correctness, security & data-loss

## P0 (4)

### BUG-001 — [P0][data-loss] Accept Plan silently deletes ALL numbered days — wiping day journals, plan text, and permanently destroying day-attached photos/documents from disk

_ai · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:447-456`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:624-626`, `src/routes/days.py:264-353`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/tripMediaModals.ts:429`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/journalingModal.ts:42`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/trip.ts:214-217`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/en.ts:1015`
- **Symptom:** A user generates an AI plan and clicks the button labeled 'Accept Plan & Add to Trip'. Every existing numbered trip day (dayNumber > 0) is deleted — including days the user hand-created via 'Add Day', days auto-scaffolded at trip creation, and AI days from a prior accept. The server delete_day cascade then (a) PERMANENTLY deletes from disk every photo/document the user attached to those days (trip-level photos_json/documents_json items whose dayId matched), and (b) tombstones the day rows, losing each day's journal entry (day.notes), per-day plan text (morning/afternoon/evening), and Expert Tip. There is NO confirmation dialog and the button verb ('Add to Trip') implies an additive, non-destructive action.
- **Root cause:** onAcceptPlan (useAiPlan.ts:450-456) does `existingNumbered = STATE.tripDays.filter(d => d.tripId === activeTrip.id && d.dayNumber > 0)` then `existingNumbered.forEach(d => deleteDayOnServer(d.id))` — it deletes EVERY numbered day regardless of origin, not just AI-created ones (there is no source/provenance check on days, unlike markedPlaces which has dropAITaggedPlaces). deleteDayOnServer hits DELETE /api/days/<id>, whose handler (days.py:264-352) runs a delete-cascade: it collects upload paths for trip-level photos_json/documents_json items with `dayId == day_id`, DROPS them from the JSON arrays, and calls delete_upload_files(upload_paths, owner_id) (days.py:351-352) which unlinks the files from disk. Photos are attached to days with the trip-day id as dayId (tripMediaModals.ts:429,782,953), and journal text is written to day.notes (journalingModal.ts:42). Because ItineraryOutput's `accepted` flag is component-local useState (ItineraryOutput.tsx:87) it resets on every remount, and the itinerary is re-shown from activeTrip.aiPlan on return to /ai — so the user can navigate away and back and re-accept, and a first-time AI user with auto-scaffolded days (modals/trip.ts:214, dayNumber starts at 1) loses everything on their FIRST accept.
- **Repro:** 1) Create a trip with the auto-scaffold-days option (or add days manually). 2) Open a day, write a journal note and attach a photo (home → day detail). 3) Go to /ai, generate a plan, click 'Accept Plan & Add to Trip'. 4) Observe in Home: the day you journaled/photographed is gone; its journal text and the photo file are permanently deleted (the photo's <img> 404s and the file is unlinked server-side). Re-running Accept Plan a second time (navigate Home → AI → Accept again) repeats the destruction on any days created by the first accept.
- **Suggested fix:** Do not blanket-delete all numbered days. Either (a) gate deletion to AI-provenance days only (add a source/origin marker on TripDay the same way markedPlaces uses source==='ai', and only delete those), or (b) show an explicit, blocking confirmation that names exactly what will be lost ('This replaces your N existing days and permanently deletes M photos and J journal entries attached to them') before any delete fires, and (c) before deleting a day client-side, detach/migrate its day-tagged photos/documents to trip-wide (null dayId) rather than relying on the server cascade to delete the files — or change delete_day to NULL the dayId of media (as it already does for markedPlaces, days.py:300-306) instead of unlinking files. Also change the button label so the verb does not imply 'add'.
- **Verifier:** onAcceptPlan (useAiPlan.ts:450-456) deletes EVERY dayNumber>0 day with no provenance guard (unlike dropAITaggedPlaces which keeps source!=='ai' places, markedPlaces.ts:347), and DELETE /api/days/<id> cascade-drops trip-level photos_json/documents_json items with dayId==day_id (days.py:313-318, drop=True) then unlinks their files from disk via delete_upload_files (days.py:351-352); itinerary re-paints from activeTrip.aiPlan on remount (useAiPlan.ts:152) and accepted is local useState (ItineraryOutput.tsx:87) so re-accept after editing days is reachable, making the disk deletion irreversible.

### BUG-002 — [P0][data-loss] Template snapshot keeps creator's source:'ai' on marked places — friend's first Accept Plan silently DELETES every imported to-do

_journey-creator-template · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `src/routes/templates.py:85-109`, `src/routes/templates.py:182-185`, `src/routes/templates.py:208-220`, `frontend/static/js/src/markedPlaces.ts:334-348`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:459`
- **Symptom:** A friend creates a trip from a creator's template code. The imported To-do list (the curated places the creator shared) appears correctly. The moment the friend runs the AI planner and taps Accept Plan, most/all of those imported to-dos vanish without warning — exactly the model bug (an AI plan silently deleting a hand-built/imported to-do list).
- **Root cause:** \_build_template_snapshot copies the creator's marked_places_json into the snapshot and only runs \_clean_marked_places, which pops ONLY dayId and timeOfDay (templates.py:85-109, 182-185). The provenance field `source` is preserved verbatim. Creators build shareable itineraries with the AI planner, so their marked places overwhelmingly carry source:'ai' (stamped by addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified, markedPlaces.ts:320). That source:'ai' is baked into the snapshot, written straight into the friend's new trip by \_instantiate_template (templates.py:208-220, which also does NOT strip source), and hydrated into STATE via fetchTripMedia. On the friend's first Accept Plan, onAcceptPlan calls dropAITaggedPlaces(activeTrip) (useAiPlan.ts:459), which deletes EVERY markedPlace whose source==='ai' (markedPlaces.ts:345-348) — i.e. all the imported template to-dos — before adding the friend's own AI items. This is the precise sibling of the recently-fixed bug where promoting a manual to-do to source:'ai' let dropAITaggedPlaces delete it; the template import path re-introduces source:'ai' items the friend never created.
- **Repro:** 1. As a creator, build a trip, run the AI planner, Accept Plan (this stamps the auto-pushed places source:'ai'). Confirm they show in the To-do list. 2. Settings → Creator → save the trip as a template with 'Marked places' included; copy the code. 3. As a DIFFERENT user, enter the code → owned trip is created; open it → imported To-do list is fully present. 4. Open the AI page, generate any plan, tap Accept Plan. 5. Observe: every imported to-do with source:'ai' is gone from the To-do list and map.
- **Suggested fix:** Normalize provenance on the way INTO a fresh trip: in \_clean_marked_places (or \_instantiate_template) set each imported place's source to 'manual' (and drop/keep forAI as desired) so imported to-dos are treated as the new owner's hand-curated items and survive dropAITaggedPlaces — mirroring the blanked-dates / stripped-dayId rationale already documented there. Equivalently, strip `source` at snapshot-build time so imported items default to manual. A server-side one-liner (q['source']='manual') in \_clean_marked_places fixes both freshly-built and already-stored templates on import.
- **Verifier:** Verified the full chain: \_clean_marked_places (templates.py:105-108) pops ONLY dayId/timeOfDay and never touches `source`; templates.py has zero references to the marked-place `source` field anywhere on snapshot or \_instantiate_template (line 220), so imported places retain source:'ai' (stamped by addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified, markedPlaces.ts:320); fetchTripMedia (media.ts:204,232) hydrates them verbatim and state.ts loadState (238-247) doesn't touch `source`; onAcceptPlan calls dropAITaggedPlaces(activeTrip) at useAiPlan.ts:459 BEFORE adding new items, and dropAITaggedPlaces (markedPlaces.ts:347) deletes every source==='ai' entry — and commit 3186648 documents this exact deletion mechanism as a real data-loss bug whose fix did NOT cover the template-import path.

### BUG-003 — [P0][data-loss] Offline outbox dedup keys on (method, url) only — collapses ALL offline edits of one resource type to a single row; the rest are silently lost

_sync-offline · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.96_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/outbox.ts:205`, `frontend/static/js/src/outbox.ts:96`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:251`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:546`, `src/routes/expenses.py:31`, `src/routes/trips.py:65`
- **Symptom:** A user who creates/edits several expenses (or trip days, budgets, trips, settlements) while offline sees all of them locally; on reconnect all but the LAST one of each resource type vanish. They were never persisted server-side and pullFromServer (api.ts:204 `STATE.expenses = data.expenses`) overwrites local state with server truth, dropping the optimistic-only rows.
- **Root cause:** enqueueMutation dedupes by `i.method === item.method && i.url === item.url` (outbox.ts:205-207). But every row-upsert POST uses a CONSTANT url with the row id in the BODY, not the URL: upsertExpense→POST /api/expenses, upsertDay→/api/days, upsertBudget→/api/budgets, upsertTrip→/api/trips, createSettlement→/api/settlements (confirmed server-side: expenses.py:47 / trips.py:82 read id from the body). So two different expenses both dedupe to key (POST,/api/expenses) and the second REPLACES the first's body (outbox.ts:208-218 keeps prev.id/enqueuedAt but takes the NEW body). Offline nothing drains, so all offline mutations pile up and collapse. The R8-B1 dedup was written to coalesce repeated edits of the SAME row but the key can't distinguish rows. DELETE is unaffected (id is in the URL: /api/expenses/<id>).
- **Repro:** 1. Go offline. 2. Add 5 different expenses via Expenses → Manual (or any batch). 3. All 5 appear in History (optimistic + localStorage). 4. Reconnect (fires the `online` drain in main.ts:317). 5. Only the 5th expense exists on the server; the next pullFromServer drops expenses 1–4 from the UI permanently. Same with creating multiple trip days offline while planning on a plane.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the dedup key row-identity-aware, not URL-only. Either (a) include a stable identity in the key derived from the body (e.g. parse body and use `${method} ${url} ${body.expense?.id ?? body.trip?.id ?? body.day?.id ?? body.budget?.id ?? body.settlement?.id}`), or (b) only dedup when that parsed id matches. Media (/api/trips/<id>/media) already has the id in the URL so it dedups correctly and should be left as-is. Add outbox unit tests (none exist).
- **Verifier:** Verified inline: api.ts:548 upsertExpense POSTs to the constant collection URL /api/expenses (id in body), api.ts:620 days→/api/days, misc.ts:91 settlements→/api/settlements; outbox.ts:205-218 dedups on (method,url) and REPLACES the prior body, so two distinct offline creates collapse to the last one.

### BUG-004 — [P0][data-loss] Offline batch CSV/Tricount/Splitwise import: entire import collapses to ONE expense in the outbox

_sync-offline · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.95_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:446`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:440`, `frontend/static/js/src/outbox.ts:205`
- **Symptom:** Importing a file of N expenses while offline (or if connectivity drops during the import) persists only the LAST expense to the server. The user sees all N locally, but after the next pullFromServer N-1 silently disappear.
- **Root cause:** applyImport loops `STATE.expenses.push(expense); void upsertExpense(expense)` per row (upload.ts:440-446) with no online gate. All rows fire near-simultaneously; offline they all enqueue to the same (POST,/api/expenses) outbox key, which dedup-collapses to the last one (see the dedup-key finding). There is no `navigator.onLine` guard on import (unlike the settle form at pages/settlement/actions.ts:111).
- **Repro:** 1. Go offline. 2. Expenses → Import a CSV with 10 rows. 3. UI shows 'Imported 10'. 4. Reconnect. 5. Server has 1 expense; pull drops the other 9 from History.
- **Suggested fix:** Fix the underlying outbox dedup key (primary). As defense-in-depth, the import could detect navigator.onLine===false and warn, or enqueue with per-row identity once the dedup key is row-aware.
- **Verifier:** Same root as the dedup bug: a bulk import fires N upsertExpense calls all to POST /api/expenses; offline they enqueue to one (method,url) key and collapse to a single row. No navigator.onLine guard on the import path.

## P1 (15)

### BUG-005 — [P1][bug] AI itinerary renders as EMPTY cards (and Accept writes '[object Object]') when the server has no Google Maps key — the documented 'graceful no-op' path is broken for the food/sights schema

_ai · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `src/routes/integrations.py:302-308`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/slots.ts:115-123`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/slots.ts:231-235`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/ItineraryOutput.tsx:290-296`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/slots.ts:290-300`
- **Symptom:** On any instance where neither GOOGLE_MAPS_SERVER_KEY nor GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY is set (a configuration the code explicitly claims to support: 'Gracefully no-ops when GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY isn't set'), AI generation succeeds and Gemini returns real restaurants/sights, but every meal card and the sights card render with their title (Breakfast/Lunch/Dinner/Sightseeing) and a completely BLANK body — the place name, why, and fact all disappear. If the user clicks Accept Plan, the day's morning/afternoon/evening plan text is written as the literal string '[object Object]'.
- **Root cause:** When no Maps key is configured, \_enrich_itinerary returns the itinerary UNCHANGED (integrations.py:307-308), so for the new food/sights schema the meal/sight objects keep their raw Gemini shape {name, why, fact} and never get a `text` field (text is only added by \_enrich_one at integrations.py:339 on the enrichment path). The frontend renderer renderSlotItem keys ENTIRELY off `text`: `const text = String(v.text || ''); if (!text) return '';` (slots.ts:122-123) — so an object with `name` but no `text` renders nothing. MealBlock's has-content guard checks `p.text || p.name` (ItineraryOutput.tsx:291) so it thinks there IS content and calls renderRestaurantCard, which then emits an empty string. On Accept, itemToText (slots.ts:231-235) falls through to `String(item ?? '')` for an object lacking a string `text`, yielding '[object Object]', which flattenMealForTextarea writes into the day plan. The legacy items[] string schema is unaffected (strings render as bullets) — only the current food/sights schema is broken without a Maps key.
- **Repro:** 1) Run the server with GEMINI_API_KEY set but no GOOGLE_MAPS_SERVER_KEY/GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY. 2) Generate an AI plan. 3) Observe each Breakfast/Lunch/Dinner card shows only its label with an empty body; the Sightseeing card is empty. 4) Click Accept Plan → open the day in Home → morning/afternoon/evening show '[object Object]'.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the no-key path still populate a usable text field. In \_enrich_itinerary's no-key early-return, normalize each meal/sight dict so it carries `text` (e.g. set item['text'] = item.get('name') before returning), OR run the dict→{text,why,fact,verified:false} normalization (the \_enrich_one base shape) even when api_key is empty (skip only the Places lookup). Alternatively make the frontend renderers fall back to `name` when `text` is absent (renderSlotItem/itemToText: `const text = String(v.text || v.name || '')`).
- **Verifier:** With no Maps key \_enrich_itinerary returns the itinerary unchanged (integrations.py:307-308) so meals keep their raw Gemini shape {name,why,fact} with no text field (prompt schema integrations.py:782-787); MealBlock's guard p.text||p.name is true because name exists (ItineraryOutput.tsx:291) and calls renderRestaurantCard→renderSlotItem which returns '' since `const text=String(v.text||''); if(!text) return ''` (slots.ts:122-123, 274) → empty card, while on Accept itemToText falls to String(item) = '[object Object]' (slots.ts:234) which flattenMealForTextarea writes (truthy, not skipped) into the day plan.

### BUG-006 — [P1][data-loss] Involuntary session-expiry (401) path leaves the previous user's trips/expenses/days/budgets in STATE and re-persists them to localStorage — shared-device privacy leak

_auth · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:82-157`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:269-291`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile.ts:49-111`, `frontend/static/js/src/state.ts:353-382`, `frontend/static/js/src/state.ts:438`
- **Symptom:** When a session ends WITHOUT the user clicking Log out — i.e. the 30-day JWT expires mid-session, the session is revoked from another device, or the server otherwise returns 401 — the user is bounced to the login wall, but STATE.trips / archivedTrips / expenses / tripDays / budgets / activities / photos / savedFormats / categories and the offline outbox are NOT cleared, and the next `state:changed` emit re-writes the full STATE (including that data) back into the `theGreatEscapeState` localStorage blob. On a shared/family device, the next person to open the app sees the prior user's trips, expense amounts, who-paid splits and itinerary in any cached-data UI until they log in and a fresh /api/data pull lands. If that next person logs in and goes back online, drainOutbox() can also replay the prior user's queued offline mutations under the new user's cookie.
- **Root cause:** The deliberate logout() in pages/profile.ts:70-101 was carefully hardened (R2 / SY7 / SY9 / R8-B3) to null out user, activeTripId, trips, archivedTrips, expenses, tripDays, budgets, activities, photos, notifications, savedFormats, categories AND clearOutbox(). But the INVOLUNTARY teardown path — apiFetch()'s 401 branch (core.ts:269-284) — only calls clearAuthToken() + sets STATE.user=null + emit. clearAuthToken() (core.ts:82-157) removes the localStorage blob and resets notifications/draftExpense/geminiApiKey/settlements/achievements/lastImportBatch/preferences/rateMode/insightCurrency, but it does NOT clear trips/archivedTrips/expenses/tripDays/budgets/activities/photos/savedFormats/categories or the outbox. Because saveState (subscribed to state:changed, state.ts:438) serializes the WHOLE STATE object 250 ms after the emit, the just-removed blob is immediately repopulated with the previous user's data. The SW cache IS cleared (CLEAR_API_CACHE / CLEAR_USER are posted from clearAuthToken), which is why this gap was missed — only the in-memory + localStorage STATE leak remains.
- **Repro:** 1. On a shared device, log in as User A; open a trip with expenses/days so STATE is populated. 2. Force an involuntary 401: wait for the 30-day JWT to expire, OR revoke A's current session from another device (Settings → Sessions), OR have the server bump A's jti. 3. On A's tab the next 15s poll (/api/sync) 401s → apiFetch clears STATE.user and navigates to the login wall. 4. Open DevTools → Application → Local Storage: `theGreatEscapeState` still contains A's trips/expenses/tripDays/budgets (re-persisted ~250 ms after the bounce). 5. Reload (or have User B sit down): loadState() loads A's trips into STATE; any cached-data surface renders A's private data before B logs in / before B's pull completes.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the involuntary teardown clear the same surface as the deliberate logout. Either (a) have clearAuthToken() additionally null trips, archivedTrips, expenses, tripDays, budgets, activities, photos, savedFormats, activeTripId, categories and call clearOutbox(); or (b) factor the full STATE wipe in logout() into a shared `wipeUserState()` and call it from BOTH logout() and the apiFetch 401 branch. Clearing must happen before the emit so saveState persists the empty state, not the stale one.
- **Verifier:** core.ts:269-291's 401 branch only calls clearAuthToken()+STATE.user=null+emit, and clearAuthToken (core.ts:118-146) resets notifications/draft/geminiKey/settlements/achievements/prefs but NOT trips/archivedTrips/expenses/tripDays/budgets/activities/photos/savedFormats/categories/outbox, while saveState (subscribed at state.ts:438) re-serializes the WHOLE STATE 250ms later (state.ts:363), re-writing the prior user's data the blob-removal just cleared.

### BUG-007 — [P1][security] Block primitive has no UI entry point — entire server-enforced safety feature is unreachable

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.95_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/feed.ts:31`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/Profile.tsx:718`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Blocks.tsx:1`, `src/routes/blocks.py:62`
- **Symptom:** A user being harassed (spam follows, comments, reposts, invites) has no way to block the harasser. There is no 'Block' button on a foreign profile, on any feed card, or in the Friends list. The Settings → Blocked-users tab can only LIST and UNBLOCK — for a normal user it is always empty because there is no way to ADD a block. The harasser remedy the whole feature was built for is effectively still 'silence your own bell.'
- **Root cause:** The frontend helper `blockUser(userId)` (api/feed.ts:31) is defined but NEVER invoked anywhere in the app — `grep` shows the only importers are api/feed.ts (definition) and Blocks.tsx (which imports only `fetchBlockedUsers` + `unblockUser`). Profile.tsx renders only `FollowButton` for foreign profiles (Profile.tsx:718-725); there is no Block control. Comments in Blocks.tsx:6 and Settings.tsx:347 reference 'a stray Block tap on a profile card' that does not exist in the codebase — the trigger was never built (or was removed) while all the server enforcement (blocks.py, follows.py:104, friends.py:155, feed_events.py block filters, explore block filter) shipped.
- **Repro:** 1) Sign in. 2) Open another user's profile (or a feed card author). 3) Look for any way to block them. There is none — only Follow/Following. 4) Open Settings → Blocked users: the list is empty with no path to populate it. The only way to block is calling POST /api/blocks/<id> by hand.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a Block action (e.g. a kebab/overflow menu next to FollowButton on Profile.tsx, and/or a menu on feed EventCard authors) that calls blockUser(); on success, navigate away / refresh and reset local follow state. This wires the existing, fully-enforced server primitive to a user-facing trigger.
- **Verifier:** grep confirms blockUser (api/feed.ts:31) has zero importers/callers; Profile.tsx renders only FollowButton for foreign profiles (line 720) and 'Log Out' for own (line 717) — no Block control, and the comments in Blocks.tsx:6 / Settings.tsx:347 reference a 'Block tap on a profile card' that does not exist, so the advertised safety primitive is genuinely unreachable from the app.

### BUG-008 — [P1][security] Stored XSS on Home dashboard via unescaped trip name in the 'expenses recorded for {trip}' stat line

_home · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HomeHeader.tsx:193-200`, `frontend/static/js/src/i18n.ts:262-267`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/en.ts:1478`, `src/routes/trips.py:84-89`, `src/routes/trips.py:195-244`
- **Symptom:** If a trip's name contains HTML (e.g. `<img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)>`), that markup is parsed and the script executes the moment the trip's Home page renders. Because trips are shareable, a member who can edit the trip name can plant a payload that fires on every other member's (including the owner's) Home dashboard — cookie/session theft, actions-as-victim, etc.
- **Root cause:** HomeHeader renders the stat line with `dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: t('home.tripStatsLine', { count: '<strong>N</strong>', trip: activeTrip.name || '' }) }}`. The t() interpolator does a plain String(params[name]) substitution with NO HTML-escaping (i18n.ts:266-267), and the {trip} slot is filled with the raw user-controlled trip name. The template uses dangerouslySetInnerHTML only to bold the count, but the same unescaped path carries activeTrip.name into the DOM as live HTML. Server-side, upsert_trip binds t['name'] straight into the INSERT with only a presence check (trips.py:88) and no sanitization, and it round-trips raw via /api/data. Sibling code escapes the name correctly — trip-controls.ts:52 uses esc(t.name), TripBody.tsx:974/979 wrap with esc(...), Collections.tsx uses plain JSX {trip.name} — so this is an inconsistency that singled out the Home stat line.
- **Repro:** 1. Create/rename a trip with the name `<img src=x onerror=alert(document.cookie)>`. 2. Make it the active trip and open Home. 3. The stat line renders the img tag; onerror fires → alert. (Cross-user: share the trip; the payload fires on the other member's Home too.)
- **Suggested fix:** Escape the name before interpolation: pass `trip: esc(activeTrip.name || '')` (utils.esc), keeping only the intentional <strong> around the already-numeric count. Better: stop using dangerouslySetInnerHTML here — render `<p>You have <strong>{count}</strong> expenses recorded for {name}.</p>` as JSX so React auto-escapes the name. Also add server-side length/HTML hardening on trip name in upsert_trip as defense-in-depth.
- **Verifier:** Verified end-to-end: t() does raw String(params[name]) with no HTML-escape (i18n.ts:266-267), HomeHeader feeds activeTrip.name raw into dangerouslySetInnerHTML (HomeHeader.tsx:194-200), the name is stored UNescaped at creation (modals/trip.ts:133 reads input .value verbatim — the Todo.tsx:455 comment claiming names are esc()'d at creation is false), and sibling sites DO escape (companions.ts:146/415, share.ts:411, tripChecklistModal.ts:94, trip-controls.ts:52), so this is a genuine inconsistency; a shared-trip planner setting a malicious name makes it cross-user (dom-helpers.ts:102 scopes esc to exactly that), justifying P1 over self-XSS — note Todo.tsx:457 carries the identical bug.

### BUG-009 — [P1][security] /api/sync bulk trip_days loop has NO authorization gate — cross-tenant day write/inject (IDOR sibling of the R2 /api/days fix)

_itinerary · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `src/routes/data.py:793-838`, `src/routes/data.py:302-306`, `src/routes/days.py:77-91`
- **Symptom:** Any authenticated user can overwrite or inject trip-day rows on a trip they do not own / are not a planner on. They can rewrite an existing day's morning/afternoon/evening/tip/notes/name/date/lat/lng (if they know its id), inject arbitrary new day rows under a victim's tripId (e.g. a second Day 0, or thousands of junk days), and bypass every per-row guard (dayNumber bounds, fractional/negative rejection, optimistic-concurrency).
- **Root cause:** The `/api/sync` trip*days loop (data.py:793-838) writes `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT(id) DO UPDATE` keyed only on `WHERE trip_days.deleted_at IS NULL`. It trusts `d['tripId']` verbatim and has NO membership check. The sibling loops in the SAME handler ARE gated: the trips loop does `if existing and t['id'] not in editable_trip_ids: continue` (data.py:302-306) and the expenses loop gates on `expense_writable_trip_ids`. The per-row POST /api/days route was hardened against exactly this (R2 fix, days.py:77-91, with test test_days_single_row_upsert_blocks_cross_trip_hijack), but the bulk-path sibling was missed. The loop also omits the dayNumber validation (negative/huge/fractional) that days.py:50-74 enforces. The first-party client now sends `{}` to /api/sync (api.ts:80), so there is no first-party trigger, but the route still accepts and writes the payload from any caller — and AI-accepted days use predictable ids `'day*'+Date.now()+'\_'+idx` (useAiPlan.ts:466), making targeted overwrites feasible even without an id leak.
- **Repro:** As user A (any logged-in account), POST /api/sync with body {"trip_days":[{"id":"<victim-day-id-or-new>","tripId":"<victim-trip-id>","dayNumber":0,"name":"PWNED","morning":"injected"}]}. The row is inserted/updated on the victim trip. No 403 is returned (handler returns {"status":"synced"}). Confirm via the victim's GET /api/data.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the trips/expenses loops: preload `editable_trip_ids = batch_editable_trip_ids(cursor, user_id)` (already computed at data.py:280) and, in the trip_days loop, skip rows whose effective trip isn't editable — for an existing day gate on its CURRENT trip_id, for a new day gate on `d['tripId']` (and reject if the user can't edit that trip). Also run the same dayNumber bounds/fractional validation as days.py. Add a test analogous to test_days_single_row_upsert_blocks_cross_trip_hijack but via /api/sync.
- **Verifier:** data.py:795-838 INSERTs/UPSERTs trip*days using d['tripId'] verbatim with the ONLY guard being `WHERE trip_days.deleted_at IS NULL` — no `if d['tripId'] not in editable_trip_ids: continue` like the trips loop (302-306) or expenses loop, and there is no test_sync*...\_trip_days_loop_blocks_cross_trip_hijack (only the per-row days route and the expenses sync loop have such tests), so any authenticated caller can overwrite/inject days on trips they don't belong to (AI day ids are predictable via useAiPlan.ts:466).

### BUG-010 — [P1][correctness] One-click 'Settle' on a no-FX-rate currency debt (ARS/EGP/VND…) fabricates a 1:1 euroValue, poisoning EUR balances, the cross-trip Global tab and Insights with a wildly inflated number

_journey-money · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:115`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/SettlementView.tsx:290-320`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/currency.ts:71-78`, `src/routes/settlements.py:205-229`, `src/fx_rates.py:215-228`
- **Symptom:** On a trip with spend in a currency that has no live/static FX rate (e.g. ARS, EGP, VND), the per-currency suggested-payments list shows a debt like 'Alice → Bob 50000 ARS' with a working Settle button. Clicking it records a settlement that the EUR-denominated views treat as €50,000: the trip's EUR balances invert, the cross-trip Global tab shows a phantom €50k debt, the History day-total and 'settled' chip jump to €50k, and Insights net-balances are skewed. The expense form blocks these currencies without a manual EUR amount, but the Settle button has no equivalent guard.
- **Root cause:** settleDebt computes `const euroValue = convertCurrency(amount, currency, 'EUR')` (actions.ts:115). For a no-rate currency convertCurrency falls back to rate 1 (currency.ts:71-78 `_rateFor` returns CONVERSION_RATES[code] || 1), so euroValue == the raw foreign amount. PATH A then POSTs {amount, currency:'ARS', euroValue:<raw>}. The server's non-EUR guard (settlements.py:222-228) only rejects when `rate is None AND euro_value is None` — here euro_value is the (bogus) raw number, so it passes; compute_euro_value's cold path returns that client hint verbatim (fx_rates.py:221-228). The settlement is stored with euro_value == raw foreign amount and counts 1:1 as EUR everywhere (applySettlementToBalances euroValue||amount, computeGlobalBalances, settlementEurForTotal, Insights netBalances). SettlementView only consults hasRate(d.currency) to decide whether to show the '≈ EUR' hint (line 302), NOT to gate the Settle button; openManualSettleModal has the same gap.
- **Repro:** 1. Trip with a companion who is a linked accepted member. 2. Add an ARS expense via the manual form, supplying the required manual EUR amount (so the expense itself is sane). 3. Settlement → Trip tab shows an ARS suggested debt. 4. Click Settle. 5. Switch the big number to EUR / open Global tab / open Insights → the settlement is counted as that many EUROS (e.g. 50000 ARS → €50,000), inverting the ledger.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate the per-currency Settle button (and openManualSettleModal submit) on hasRate(currency): for no-rate currencies, route through a manual-EUR prompt (mirroring the expense/budget manual-EUR flow) instead of silently calling convertCurrency 1:1. Defensively, settleDebt should not pass a 1:1 euroValue for a no-rate currency, and the server gate (settlements.py:222) should reject a non-EUR settlement whose euroValue equals the raw amount when no live rate exists (i.e. require a real conversion, matching the expense C1 gate in expenses.py:134-145).
- **Verifier:** settleDebt always computes euroValue = convertCurrency(amount,currency,'EUR') (actions.ts:115), which for a no-rate code returns amount\*1/1 = the raw foreign amount (\_rateFor falls back to 1, currency.ts:71-78), and the Settle button is gated only on the in-flight 'settling' flag, never on hasRate (SettlementView.tsx:311-320 vs the hint-only hasRate at :302); the server allows 41 currencies incl. ARS/EGP/VND/CLP/COP/PEN (validators.py:68) while Frankfurter (fx_rates.py:58) supplies no rate for them, so compute_euro_value's cold path returns the bogus client hint verbatim (fx_rates.py:217-232) and the guard passes because euro_value is never None (settlements.py:222-228) — the 1:1 value then feeds applySettlementToBalances euroValue||amount (balances.ts:92) and computeGlobalBalances (balances.ts:587), corrupting EUR balances/Global/Insights.

### BUG-011 — [P1][security] Share-token clone copies day-plan text even when share_show_plans=0, bypassing the public-page plan gate

_journey-share-clone · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:1384`, `src/routes/trips.py:1407`, `src/routes/trips.py:1554`, `src/routes/public.py:591`, `src/routes/public.py:615`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/share.ts:148`
- **Symptom:** An owner shares a trip with the "Show day plans" toggle OFF (the default). The public /share/<token> page deliberately renders only day names/dates and hides the morning/afternoon/evening/tip text. But when any recipient (a logged-out stranger who then signs up) clicks "I want this trip", their cloned copy contains the FULL plan text for every day — the exact private content the owner chose not to expose on the shared page. The privacy toggle the owner relied on is silently bypassed by the very next step in the journey.
- **Root cause:** `fetch_share_payload` (public.py:591-622) gates the plan SELECT and the per-day `plan`/`tip` attachment on `show_plans = bool(row['share_show_plans'])` — so a share with `share_show_plans=0` (DEFAULT 0 in database.py:268; share modal defaults `showPlans:false`, share.ts:148) never sends plan text to the viewer. However the clone path does NOT honour that flag: `clone_trip_from_share_token` (trips.py:1515) calls `_clone_trip_record(cursor, row['id'], user_id)` with no privacy argument, and `_clone_trip_record` (trips.py:1384-1425) unconditionally SELECTs `morning, afternoon, evening, tip` and INSERTs them into the clone's trip_days. The clone copies the source rows directly from the DB, ignoring the share_show_plans gate that governs what the recipient was actually shown.
- **Repro:** 1. User A creates a trip, fills in plan text for each day. 2. A opens Share → Get share link, leaves both toggles OFF, generates the link. 3. Open /share/<token> logged-out: confirm only day names/dates show, NO plan text. 4. Click "I want this trip", sign in as User B (a stranger). 5. Open the cloned trip in B's Collections → every day's morning/afternoon/evening/tip text from A's private plan is present, despite never being visible on the shared page.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread the source trip's `share_show_plans` into `_clone_trip_record` and, when it is 0, NULL out morning/afternoon/evening/tip on the cloned days (copy only day_number/name/lat/lng) — matching exactly what the share page exposed. The structural cloning model should copy only what the recipient was authorized to SEE, not the raw source rows.
- **Verifier:** fetch_share_payload gates the morning/afternoon/evening/tip SELECT + per-day attachment on bool(row['share_show_plans']) (public.py:591,615-621) with DB DEFAULT 0 (database.py:268), but clone_trip_from_share_token (trips.py:1554) calls \_clone_trip_record with no privacy arg and \_clone_trip_record unconditionally SELECTs+INSERTs morning/afternoon/evening/tip (trips.py:1385,1407-1425), so a recipient shown only the skeleton can clone to obtain the deliberately-withheld plan text.

### BUG-012 — [P1][security] Clone copies the owner's full markedPlaces wishlist, which the share page and public-trip read both strip from non-members

_journey-share-clone · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:1309`, `src/routes/trips.py:1346`, `src/routes/public.py:203`, `src/routes/public.py:490`, `frontend/static/js/src/types.d.ts:298`
- **Symptom:** A stranger who clones a shared (or public) trip receives the owner's entire markedPlaces array verbatim — place names, reverse-geocoded addresses, AI-generated "why this place"/"surprising fact" annotations, day assignments, and forAI/forManual flags (MarkedPlace shape, types.d.ts:298). This wishlist is NEVER shown on the /share/<token> page (fetch_share_payload doesn't even SELECT marked_places_json) and is explicitly stripped for non-members on /api/public-trip (public.py:203 sets `trip['markedPlaces']=[]`). The recipient ends up owning private planning data the product never surfaced to them.
- **Root cause:** `_clone_trip_attempt` (trips.py:1309) copies `src['marked_places_json']` directly into the clone with the comment "copied verbatim (the user's wishlist of places is half the value of cloning)". This deliberate copy contradicts the share/public-trip privacy contract: both read surfaces treat markedPlaces as owner-private. The clone is the only surface that hands the wishlist to a non-member, and it does so unconditionally for both clone entry points.
- **Repro:** 1. User A builds a trip with several marked places (with AI why/fact text and addresses). 2. A shares the trip via link (plans toggle irrelevant — markedPlaces is never gated). 3. Stranger B clones via "I want this trip". 4. B opens the cloned trip's to-do/marked-places list → A's full wishlist with addresses + AI annotations is present, though B never saw it on the shared page.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the intended contract and make clone consistent with the read surfaces. If markedPlaces is private (as share + public-trip treat it), do NOT copy marked_places_json on clone (set it to None like documents/photos/checklist). If sharing the wishlist is genuinely the intended value, surface it on the share page too so the recipient sees what they're cloning — but copying data that was deliberately hidden from the viewer is the leak.
- **Verifier:** \_clone_trip_attempt copies src['marked_places_json'] verbatim (trips.py:1309) while /api/public-trip sets trip['markedPlaces']=[] for non-members (public.py:203) and fetch_share_payload never includes markedPlaces at all; since \_caller_can_see_trip grants cloning of any is_public trip without membership (trips.py:1458), the clone hands a non-member the entire wishlist both read surfaces withhold.

### BUG-013 — [P1][data-loss] EU-locale CSV import (semicolon delimiter + decimal comma) silently shatters every rate into garbage

_rates-editor · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.95_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:473-478`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:509-546`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/manualRates.ts:218-238`
- **Symptom:** A user in a European locale (the founder's primary market is Portugal / pt-PT) downloads the rates template, opens it in Excel, edits, and re-saves as CSV. Excel writes EU-locale CSV: semicolon delimiters and decimal commas, e.g. `Currency;2021;2020 / USD;0,88;0,90`. On import the app shows a green 'Imported N values — review, then Save' and, after Save, the Insights 'Spent' / 'Worth today' figures are wildly wrong (e.g. 1 USD = 88 EUR). No error is shown because the parse 'succeeds' with corrupt numbers.
- **Root cause:** RatesEditor.parseCsv splits each line on the regex /[,;\t]/ (line 478). For a EU-locale cell like `0,88` the comma is the DECIMAL separator, but the split treats it as a field delimiter, so `USD;0,88;0,90` becomes ['USD','0','88','0','90']. parseRatesGrid then maps the year columns onto the shards: USD/2020 = 88, GBP/2021 = 1, GBP/2020 = 17 (empirically confirmed via probe). The locale-aware decimal-comma logic in manualRates.parseRateAmount is defeated because parseCsv has already torn the comma out before parseRatesGrid sees the cell. The .xlsx path (SheetJS typed cells) is immune, but the .csv path — which is exactly what 'Download template' produces and what most users round-trip — is broken for every comma-decimal locale (pt/es/fr/de…).
- **Repro:** 1. Home currency EUR. Settings → Personalization → Exchange rates. 2. Click 'Download template' (or just craft a CSV). 3. Open in Excel with a EU locale and 'Save as CSV' (or hand-make `Currency;2021;2020\nUSD;0,88;0,90`). 4. Import it. 5. Observe 'Imported 2 values' (success). 6. Click Save, open Insights in 'Worth today' / look at a USD expense → home value is ~100x too high (1 USD treated as 88 EUR).
- **Suggested fix:** Detect the delimiter per file instead of splitting on all of [,;\t] at once: if a line contains a semicolon, split on ';' (and treat ',' as decimal — let parseRateAmount handle it); else split on ',' (or tab). A minimal heuristic: choose ';' as the delimiter when the header row has more ';' than ',', otherwise ','. Also make the downloaded template use ';' + decimal-comma when getIntlLocale() is a comma-decimal locale (or, more robustly, emit a real .xlsx). Add a manualRates/RatesEditor unit test for `Currency;2021;2020 / USD;0,88;0,90`.
- **Verifier:** parseCsv (RatesEditor.tsx:478) splits each line on /[,;\t]/ BEFORE parseRatesGrid runs, so the locale-aware decimal-comma logic in manualRates.parseRateAmount never sees an intact `0,88` cell — a EU-locale Excel CSV (`USD;0,88;0,90`) is split into ['USD','0','88','0','90'] and mapped onto the wrong year columns; the .xlsx typed-cell path is immune; bounded to Insights display overrides per the money invariant but silently corrupts every imported rate for comma-decimal locales with no error shown.

### BUG-014 — [P1][data-loss] No-rate-currency settle silently fabricates a 1:1 euroValue — corrupts EUR/Global/Insights balances (or hard-blocks settling a real exotic-currency debt)

_settlements · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:115`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/SettlementView.tsx:290`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/currency.ts:71`, `src/routes/settlements.py:211`, `src/routes/settlements.py:222`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:376`
- **Symptom:** Two failure modes depending on the trip's recorded EUR spend. (A) On a trip whose expenses were entered correctly in a no-rate currency (the expense form FORCES a manual EUR value, so euro_value is right and total_spend is a small real number, e.g. €50 for a 50000 ARS dinner): the suggested-payment row says 'X → Y 50000 ARS' and clicking Settle posts euroValue=50000, which the server's spend-cap (total_spend\*1.01+0.5 ≈ €51) REJECTS with 'This settlement is larger than what's still outstanding for this trip' — the user can never settle a perfectly valid ARS debt through the button. (B) On a low/zero-EUR-spend trip (off-app cash debt logged after the fact, zero-spend ceiling = €1,000,000): the same 50000-ARS settle SUCCEEDS but is stored with euro_value=50000, so the EUR per-person balance, the cross-trip Global tab, the settled-total chip, and Insights all read €50,000 of phantom settlement. Either way the settle flow is broken for exotic currencies.
- **Root cause:** settleDebt (actions.ts:115) unconditionally computes `euroValue = convertCurrency(amount, currency, 'EUR')`. For a no-rate currency, convertCurrency → \_rateFor (currency.ts:71-78) falls through to `CONVERSION_RATES[upper] || 1` = 1 on BOTH sides, so it returns the raw foreign amount unchanged (50000 ARS → €50000). It then always spreads that fabricated euroValue into the POST. Server create_settlement only rejects a no-rate non-EUR settlement when `rate is None AND euro_value is None` (settlements.py:222-228); because the client always sends a (wrong) euroValue, that gate never fires, and compute_euro_value's cold path (fx_rates.py:228) just returns the client hint verbatim. The expense form has the correct pattern — `needsManualEuro = !!selCurrency && !hasRate(selCurrency)` (ManualTab.tsx:108) forces an explicit EUR amount for no-rate currencies — but the settlement modal and the one-click Settle button have NO such gate. The suggested-debt Settle button (SettlementView.tsx:310-320) renders for every currency gated only on tripIsEditable; `hasRate(d.currency)` at line 302 controls only the cosmetic '≈ EUR' hint, not the button.
- **Repro:** 1) Create a trip; add a companion linked to a second account (so PATH A / server settlement is taken). 2) Add an expense in ARS (e.g. value 50000 ARS) — the form makes you type the EUR value (say €50). 3) Open the Settle tab: a suggested row shows '... 50000 ARS' with a Settle button (no '≈ €' hint because ARS has no rate). 4) Click Settle → toast 'Settlement failed: This settlement is larger than what's still outstanding…' (cap rejects it; the ARS debt can never be cleared). 5) Variant B: on a trip with NO recorded expenses, open the manual settle modal, pick ARS (offered because… actually for zero-spend the modal falls back to home; to hit B add one tiny ARS expense so ARS is offered, keep EUR spend ~0), settle 50000 ARS → 201, and the Global tab now shows €50,000 of debt for that person.
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror the expense form's no-rate handling in the settle flow: when `!hasRate(currency)`, do NOT auto-derive euroValue from convertCurrency (which is a silent 1:1). Either (a) add a required manual-EUR field to the manual settle modal (and refuse the one-click suggested Settle for no-rate currencies, prompting the user to use the manual modal), passing that explicit euroValue, or (b) at minimum stop fabricating: send euroValue:null for no-rate currencies so the server's existing S2 gate (settlements.py:224) rejects with 'euroValue is required for non-EUR settlements' rather than recording a 1:1 figure. Also consider tightening the server: reject a non-EUR settlement whose euro_value equals its raw amount when no live rate exists (the tell-tale of a 1:1 fabrication).
- **Verifier:** settleDebt unconditionally does convertCurrency(amount,currency,'EUR') (actions.ts:115) which for a no-rate currency like ARS — confirmed in \_ALLOWED_CURRENCIES (validators.py:73) but absent from static CONVERSION_RATES (17 codes, no ARS) and from the ECB/Frankfurter live feed — falls through \_rateFor to 1/1 and returns the raw foreign amount as euroValue; it always spreads that into the POST so the server reject gate (`rate is None AND euro_value is None`, settlements.py:224) never fires and compute_euro_value's cold path returns the client hint verbatim (fx_rates.py:228), while ManualTab.tsx:108 has the correct needsManualEuro=!hasRate gate the settle modal and one-click Settle button (SettlementView.tsx:302/310) lack; P1 not P0 because it requires an exotic no-rate currency.

### BUG-015 — [P1][security] Clone-from-share copies full day-plan text, silently bypassing the owner's "Show day-by-day plans" privacy toggle

_sharing · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:1519`, `src/routes/trips.py:1384`, `src/routes/trips.py:1407`, `src/routes/public.py:591`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/en.ts`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/share.ts:147`
- **Symptom:** An owner shares a trip via link with the "Show day-by-day plans" toggle OFF (the default). The public /share/<token> page correctly hides all morning/afternoon/evening notes + tips. But the same page's first-class "I want this trip" button clones the trip, and the clone contains EVERY word of the owner's per-day plan text and tips — content the owner explicitly chose not to expose. The recipient reads the hidden plans by cloning.
- **Root cause:** fetch_share_payload (public.py:591-621) gates plan SELECT/render on share_show_plans, but the clone path does NOT. clone_trip_from_share_token (trips.py:1519) calls the shared \_clone_trip_record, which unconditionally SELECTs morning/afternoon/evening/tip (trips.py:1384-1389) and INSERTs them into the new trip's days (trips.py:1407-1425). The function takes no plan-gating parameter and never reads share_show_plans. The Share modal markets the toggle as a privacy control (en.ts togglePlansBody: 'Morning / afternoon / evening notes per day. Photos and documents stay private.'), so the bypass directly violates the stated contract.
- **Repro:** 1) As owner, open a trip with detailed morning/afternoon/evening notes. 2) Share → Get share link, leave 'Show day-by-day plans' OFF. 3) Open /share/<token> in a logged-out browser → confirm NO plan text is visible. 4) Click 'I want this trip', sign in as a different user. 5) Open the freshly cloned trip → every day's morning/afternoon/evening note and tip is present, despite the toggle being off.
- **Suggested fix:** Plumb share_show_plans into \_clone_trip_record for the share-token caller: when the source was reached via a share token whose share_show_plans=0, INSERT NULL for morning/afternoon/evening/tip (copy only day name + pin), mirroring fetch_share_payload's gate. Simplest: add an include_plans flag to \_clone_trip_record, pass row['share_show_plans'] from clone_trip_from_share_token (select it alongside is_archived). Leave clone_trip (owned/public-trip path) copying plans, since /api/public-trip already exposes plan text for is_public trips.
- **Verifier:** \_clone_trip_record SELECTs and INSERTs morning/afternoon/evening/tip unconditionally (trips.py:1384-1425) and neither clone endpoint reads share_show_plans (grep shows it only exists in the share-CREATE path at trips.py:1192-1233), while fetch_share_payload gates plan render on show_plans (public.py:591-621); since the CTA and clone_trip_from_share_token are reachable regardless of the toggle, a recipient of a plans-hidden share gets the full plan text — directly defeating the en.ts privacy claim 'Show day-by-day plans / ... Photos and documents stay private' (en.ts:1684-1685).

### BUG-016 — [P1][data-loss] Trip-media hydration Maps (\_mediaLoadedTrips/\_mediaVersion/\_pendingMedia) survive logout → shared-device media loss + hidden media on shared trips

_state · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.74_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:27`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:47`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:80`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:266`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:317`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:82`
- **Symptom:** On a shared device: User A opens shared trip T (its media hydrates, so T's id lands in \_mediaLoadedTrips and its version in \_mediaVersion). User A logs out / 401s; User B (also a member of T) logs in. B's /api/data merge gives T placeholder []-media (api.ts:178-181, because B has no prior STATE copy of T), and pullFromServer SKIPS re-hydration (api.ts:317 `!_mediaLoadedTrips.has(activeTripId)` is false — the set is stale from A). So B sees trip T with NO photos/documents/marked places/checklist even though the server has them. Worse: any metadata edit B makes (rename trip, edit companions, add a checklist item, pin a place) calls upsertTrip → persistTripMedia, whose hydration guard `_mediaLoadedTrips.has(trip.id)` is stale-TRUE, so it force-writes B's empty []-arrays over the server's real media via \_postTripMedia — wiping the trip's media for every member.
- **Root cause:** \_mediaLoadedTrips (Set), \_mediaVersion (Map) and \_pendingMedia (Map) are module-level singletons in api/media.ts and are NEVER cleared on logout — clearAuthToken() (api/core.ts:82) and pages/profile.ts logout reset STATE + the SW cache but never call .clear() on these. They key purely by tripId, with no user binding, so a tripId User A loaded stays 'loaded' for User B. Two consequences chain: (a) pullFromServer's cold-hydrate guard (api.ts:317) treats T as already hydrated for B and never GETs the real media, leaving B's STATE on the []-placeholder; (b) persistTripMedia's safety gate (media.ts:274), which exists specifically to stop []-placeholders from clobbering server media, is bypassed because the stale set says T is hydrated — so the placeholder write proceeds.
- **Repro:** Two app members A and B of the same trip T, one browser. 1. A logs in, opens T (media shows, \_mediaLoadedTrips now has T). 2. A logs out. 3. B logs in; B has never opened T this session. 4. Observe T renders with empty Photos/Documents/To-do/Checklist tabs. 5. B renames T or adds one checklist item (upsertTrip fires). 6. Re-pull / open T on any device → T's photos/documents/markedPlaces/checklist are gone server-side.
- **Suggested fix:** Clear the media-tracking singletons on every account boundary. Export a resetMediaTracking() from api/media.ts that does \_mediaLoadedTrips.clear(); \_mediaVersion.clear(); \_pendingMedia.clear(), and call it from clearAuthToken() (so both logout and the 401 path cover it). Defense-in-depth: also key these maps by `${userId}:${tripId}`, or have pullFromServer force a fetchTripMedia for the active trip when the logged-in user id changed since the last pull.
- **Verifier:** grep confirms .clear() is NEVER called on the three module-level singletons (media.ts:27/47/80) and neither clearAuthToken (core.ts) nor profile.ts logout touches them, so on a shared trip after A→B on one device the stale \_mediaLoadedTrips.has(T) makes pullFromServer skip fetchTripMedia (api.ts:317) leaving B on the []-placeholder (consequence a), and persistTripMedia's hydration gate (media.ts:274) is bypassed so a placeholder write with A's still-matching \_mediaVersion clobbers the server media (consequence b) — genuine data-loss, though gated on the narrow shared-device + shared-trip + matching-version race.

### BUG-017 — [P1][data-loss] Offline media deletes (to-do place removal, 'Clear all', photo/document delete) are silently undone — union-merge can only ADD items back, never remove

_sync-offline · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:62`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:274`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:207`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/todo/Todo.tsx:408`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/todo/Todo.tsx:432`
- **Symptom:** User opens the app offline (e.g. on a plane), deletes a to-do/marked place or taps 'Clear all', or deletes a trip photo/document. After reconnecting, the deleted item(s) reappear — the delete is silently reverted.
- **Root cause:** When a trip's media isn't hydrated in THIS tab (`_mediaLoadedTrips` is in-memory and empty after every page reload), persistTripMedia PARKS the snapshot in `_pendingMedia` and never enqueues an outbox write (media.ts:274-286). On reconnect, fetchTripMedia union-merges the parked snapshot onto server media via \_mergeMediaField, which is `out = [...serverItems]` then appends only parked items the server lacks (media.ts:62-73) — it can ONLY add, never remove. A delete is represented as an ABSENCE in the parked snapshot, so the still-present server item survives the union and is resurrected. The TRIP-1 comment's assumption 'the only possible edit is an ADD — nothing is loaded yet to delete' is false: STATE.trips media (checklist/markedPlaces/photos) is restored from localStorage by loadState() (state.ts:136), so the user can fully see and delete items while \_mediaLoadedTrips is empty. 'Clear all' (markedPlaces=[]) parks an empty array → union with server = every server place restored.
- **Repro:** 1. While online, open a trip and load its to-do list (so it's in localStorage). 2. Reload the page OFFLINE (now \_mediaLoadedTrips is empty). 3. Delete a to-do place (Todo.tsx handleRemove) or tap Clear all. 4. Item disappears locally. 5. Reconnect; fetchTripMedia runs union-merge → the deleted place(s) reappear. If the tab is closed before reconnect, the delete is dropped entirely instead.
- **Suggested fix:** Capture offline media DELETES as real outbox mutations (a force-write of the post-delete full snapshot to /api/trips/<id>/media), not just a parked union-snapshot — i.e. when persistTripMedia is called unhydrated, still enqueue the full snapshot through apiFetch so the replay (token stripped → force write) overwrites the column. Alternatively, only union-merge ADDED keys and apply removals against a known baseline; but the safest fix is to route every media write (add or delete) through the outbox so last-write-wins force-replay actually persists deletions.
- **Verifier:** Consistent with media.ts: \_mergeMediaField is add-only (out=[...server] then append parked items server lacks), and the cold-window park path never represents deletions; STATE media is restored from localStorage so a user can delete while \_mediaLoadedTrips is empty, after which the union re-adds the server copy.

### BUG-018 — [P1][data-loss] Template-imported AI to-do places (source:'ai') are silently DELETED on the new owner's first Accept Plan

_templates · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/templates.py:85-109`, `src/routes/templates.py:208-261`, `frontend/static/js/src/markedPlaces.ts:296-348`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:447-459`
- **Symptom:** A user creates a trip from a shared template that came with a curated to-do list. The places appear in their To-do tab as if they were their own. The moment the user runs the AI planner once and taps "Accept plan", every template-supplied place that the creator had originally added via the AI planner silently vanishes from the to-do list. Only places the new owner added by hand survive. No warning, no undo.
- **Root cause:** This is a direct sibling of the just-fixed Accept-Plan/markedPlaces data-loss bug. A creator who builds an itinerary with the AI planner gets markedPlaces stamped `source:'ai'` AND `forManual:true` (markedPlaces.ts:314-320 in addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified) — so they show in the to-do list. \_build_template_snapshot/\_clean_marked_places (templates.py:85-109,182-186) copy every field EXCEPT dayId/timeOfDay, so `source:'ai'` is preserved verbatim into the snapshot. \_instantiate_template (templates.py:220,251) re-runs \_clean_marked_places and writes the places straight into the new trip's marked_places_json with `source:'ai'` intact. The new owner has no idea these are 'ai'-tagged. On their first Accept Plan, useAiPlan.ts:459 calls dropAITaggedPlaces(activeTrip) which filters out EVERY `source==='ai'` place (markedPlaces.ts:345-348) — deleting the imported template content. The recent fix only stopped addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified from PROMOTING a manual place to 'ai'; it did nothing for places that arrive already stamped 'ai' from a template (or clone — \_clone_trip_record copies marked_places_json verbatim too, trips.py:1307-1309).
- **Repro:** 1) As a creator, build a trip itinerary using the AI planner and Accept it (this stamps the to-do places source:'ai'). 2) Settings -> Creator -> publish a template of that trip with 'places' included. 3) As any other user, use the code (new-trip modal 'Create from a template code' or the /t/<code> 'Use this template' CTA) to create a trip. 4) Confirm the To-do tab shows the imported places. 5) Open the AI planner, generate any plan, tap 'Accept plan'. 6) Return to the To-do tab — the imported places are gone.
- **Suggested fix:** Normalize provenance when content crosses an ownership boundary: in \_clean_marked_places (or at the snapshot/instantiate boundary) drop or rewrite `source` to 'manual' (and clear forAI if desired) so imported to-dos are treated as the new owner's hand-curated list and survive dropAITaggedPlaces. The same normalization should be applied to \_clone_trip_record's verbatim marked_places_json copy. This mirrors how checklist completion is already reset and dayId/timeOfDay are already stripped at this boundary.
- **Verifier:** Verified the full chain: addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified stamps source:'ai'+forManual:true (markedPlaces.ts:314-320) and Accept Plan persists them via upsertTrip (useAiPlan.ts:532/543/558/563); \_clean_marked_places only pops dayId/timeOfDay so source:'ai' survives into the snapshot (templates.py:106-107) and is re-written into the new trip by \_instantiate_template (templates.py:220,251); the new owner's first Accept Plan calls dropAITaggedPlaces which filters out EVERY source==='ai' place (useAiPlan.ts:459, markedPlaces.ts:347), and the recent fix (commit 3186648) only stopped the promote-to-'ai' path (markedPlaces.ts:262-271), not pre-stamped imports — clone copies marked_places_json verbatim too (trips.py:1309), so the sibling vector is real; scoped to AI-tagged to-dos and triggered only by running the planner, hence P1 not P0.

### BUG-019 — [P1][data-loss] Clean-slate / remove of a to-do place is silently reverted during the post-load 'cold' media window (deletes lose to the additive merge)

_todo · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.78_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:37`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:62`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:207`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:266`, `frontend/static/js/src/state.ts:119`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/todo/Todo.tsx:422`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/todo/Todo.tsx:408`
- **Symptom:** A user opens (or hard-refreshes onto) the To-do page, sees their full to-do list (rehydrated from localStorage), and taps 'Clean slate' (or the ✕ on a row). The confirm fires, the 'List cleared' toast shows, the rows disappear — then a moment later every item reappears. The delete was silently undone. Same for removing a single place.
- **Root cause:** saveState() persists the whole STATE (incl. trip.markedPlaces) to localStorage, so on load loadState() shows the full to-do list before media is hydrated. But `_mediaLoadedTrips` is an in-memory Set that starts empty after every reload, so persistTripMedia() (media.ts:274) treats the trip as un-hydrated: it PARKS the write in `_pendingMedia` and calls fetchTripMedia. fetchTripMedia then does `_mergeMediaField(serverMedia.markedPlaces, pending.markedPlaces)` (media.ts:217) which is UNION-by-key — server items always survive, the parked snapshot only ADDS. A clean-slate parks `markedPlaces: []`, so the merge returns the full server array (every item resurrected) and flushes it back, also re-emitting STATE_CHANGED so the UI repaints the items the user just deleted. The guarding comment (media.ts:44 'During a cold window the only possible edit is an ADD — nothing is loaded yet to delete') is false: localStorage rehydration means items ARE visible and deletable before media loads.
- **Repro:** 1. Add a few places to a trip's to-do list; let it sync. 2. Hard-refresh the app while on (or deep-link to) #/todo, or open on a slow connection. 3. Immediately (before the GET /api/trips/<id>/media round-trip resolves) click 'Clean slate' and confirm (or click ✕ on a row). 4. Observe the toast + empty list, then the items snap back when media hydration completes. The deletion never reaches the server.
- **Suggested fix:** Deletes can't be represented as an additive union. Either (a) gate the destructive to-do actions (handleClearAll/handleRemove) and the AI-page remove until `_mediaLoadedTrips.has(trip.id)` (disable/spinner the buttons until hydrated), or (b) when a parked write removes items relative to localStorage, treat the parked snapshot as authoritative for deletions (e.g. carry a tombstone set of removed placeIds through \_pendingMedia and subtract them after the union), or (c) force a fetchTripMedia + await before allowing the first destructive media edit. Also correct the media.ts:44 comment.

## P2 (50)

### BUG-020 — [P2][correctness] Re-running Accept Plan orphans manually day-assigned places (dangling dayId) — they silently drop out of their day and fall into 'Unsorted'

_ai · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.75_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:466`, `frontend/static/js/src/markedPlaces.ts:259-260`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/tripMediaModals.ts:97-107`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/dayDetailModal.ts:350-356`
- **Symptom:** A user adds places to their to-do list and assigns some to specific days (via the day dropdown on the AI to-do panel or home InfoWindow). They run Accept Plan again (e.g. to regenerate after editing dates). Any manually-assigned place that the NEW AI plan does not also include keeps pointing at a day id that no longer exists — it disappears from that day's plan pane and reappears as 'Unsorted/Anytime', losing the user's day assignment with no notice.
- **Root cause:** Each Accept Plan run mints brand-new day ids (`'day_' + Date.now() + '_' + idx`, useAiPlan.ts:466) and deletes the old days. addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified only re-stamps the dayId of places that appear in the new plan (markedPlaces.ts:259). A manual place whose placeId isn't in the new plan retains its old dayId, which now references a deleted day. The day-detail and media-grouping code filter by `dayId === day.id` (dayDetailModal.ts:354) and bucket unmatched dayIds as '**orphan**'/Unsorted (tripMediaModals.ts:97), so the assignment is effectively lost.
- **Repro:** 1) Add place X to to-do, assign it to Day 3. 2) Run Accept Plan (X not in the new plan, or run twice). 3) Old Day 3 is deleted and a new Day 3 with a new id is created. 4) Place X still has the old day id → it no longer shows under any day and surfaces as Unsorted.
- **Suggested fix:** When replacing days, remap marked-place dayIds from old→new day ids by dayNumber (build an oldDayId→newDayId map keyed on matching dayNumber and re-stamp surviving manual places), or NULL the dayId of any place whose dayId no longer resolves so the state is at least consistent and the user is told. Better: reuse stable day ids across accepts (key by dayNumber) instead of regenerating them.
- **Verifier:** Each Accept mints new day ids 'day*'+Date.now()+'*'+idx and deletes the old days (useAiPlan.ts:456,466); addOrUpdatePlaceFromVerified only re-stamps dayId for places in the new plan (`existing.dayId = dayId ?? existing.dayId`, markedPlaces.ts:259), and the server's day-delete cascade NULLs the dayId of detached markedPlaces (days.py:300-305, drop=False), so a manual place not in the new plan lands in Unsorted/**orphan** per the dayId===day.id filters (dayDetailModal.ts:354, tripMediaModals.ts:97).

### BUG-021 — [P2][bug] isCreator omitted from /api/auth/google login response → Creator tab/card invisible to non-admin Creators until a full page reload

_auth · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `src/routes/auth.py:259-278`, `src/routes/auth.py:64-84`, `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/auth.ts:58`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:78-80`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:259`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:371`
- **Symptom:** A user who has been granted Creator status (users.is_creator = 1) but is NOT the hardcoded admin email logs in via Google and goes to Settings — the 'Creator' card / tab (Trip Templates publishing) is missing. It only appears after they hard-reload the page. The exact users the Creator feature is built for can't reach it right after the action (login) that should unlock it.
- **Root cause:** The login response in /api/auth/google (auth.py:259-278) builds the `user` object WITHOUT an `isCreator` field, whereas /api/user-status (the boot/reload probe, auth.py:64-84) computes and returns `isCreator`. handleGoogleLogin sets `STATE.user = data.user` (auth.ts:58), so after a fresh login STATE.user.isCreator is undefined. isCreatorUser() = `!!STATE.user?.isCreator || isAdminUser()` (Settings.tsx:78-80) is therefore false for a non-admin creator. Neither pullFromServer nor /api/data re-hydrate STATE.user or carry is_creator, so the value stays undefined until the next boot calls restoreSession()→/api/user-status, which is the only place isCreator is populated.
- **Repro:** 1. As admin, grant a second account Creator (Settings → Developer → Make Creator). 2. Sign out; sign in fresh as that second (non-admin) account via Google. 3. Go to Settings — no Creator card/tab. 4. Reload the page — Creator card/tab now appears.
- **Suggested fix:** Add the same isCreator computation to the /api/auth/google success response (and the test-login response) that /api/user-status uses: `is_creator = bool(row['is_creator']) or email.lower() in ADMIN_EMAILS`, then include `"isCreator": is_creator` in the returned user object. (Alternatively, have restoreSession-style hydration also run after login, but matching the two response shapes is the smaller fix.)
- **Verifier:** The /api/auth/google response user object (auth.py:262-275) has no isCreator field whereas /api/user-status (auth.py:82) does; STATE.user=data.user at auth.ts:58 (login) vs auth.ts:182 (restoreSession) are the ONLY two STATE.user reassignments and /api/data never touches it, so isCreatorUser() = !!STATE.user?.isCreator||isAdmin (Settings.tsx:79) is false for a non-admin creator until next boot, hiding the Creator tab (Settings.tsx:259) and card (Settings.tsx:371).

### BUG-022 — [P2][correctness] auth_sessions rows are never reaped once their JWT expires (only revoked rows are swept) → Sessions UI lists phantom dead devices and the table grows unbounded

_auth · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/auth.py:339-375`, `src/auth.py:176-216`, `src/main.py:791-799`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:128-205`
- **Symptom:** The Settings → Sessions panel shows one entry for every login the user has ever made that wasn't explicitly revoked — including sessions whose 30-day JWT has long since expired and can no longer authenticate. A user who opens the app daily for months sees dozens of 'active' devices that are actually dead, with no way to tell which are real. The auth_sessions table also grows by one row per login forever.
- **Root cause:** issue_token()→_create_session() inserts a NEW auth_sessions row on every single login (auth.py:176-216) and nothing ever deletes a session purely because its JWT expired. list_sessions (auth.py:357-363) selects `WHERE user_id = ? AND revoked_at IS NULL` with NO created_at/expiry filter, so every never-revoked row is returned regardless of whether its token is still valid. The background sweep in \_cleanup_feed_orphans (main.py:795-798) only deletes rows where `revoked_at IS NOT NULL AND revoked_at < now-30d` — it never touches expired-but-unrevoked rows. (Most logouts revoke just the current session and most expirations revoke nothing, so the un-revoked population dominates.)
- **Repro:** 1. Log in, then close the tab WITHOUT clicking Log out (so the session is never revoked). 2. Repeat several times (each is a fresh login → a fresh auth_sessions row). 3. Open Settings → Sessions: every login appears as an active device, including ones older than 30 days whose JWT has expired and which can no longer authenticate.
- **Suggested fix:** Filter list_sessions by token lifetime (e.g. `AND created_at > datetime('now','-30 days')`, matching JWT_LIFETIME_DAYS) so expired sessions drop off the UI, and extend the background sweep to also `DELETE FROM auth_sessions WHERE revoked_at IS NULL AND created_at < datetime('now','-30 days')` so the table doesn't grow unbounded. Consider also capping rows per user (revoke/delete the oldest beyond N) on each login.
- **Verifier:** \_create_session inserts a new row per login with no expiry (auth.py:199-203), the JWT has a finite 30-day exp (auth.py:253), list_sessions selects WHERE user_id=? AND revoked_at IS NULL with no created_at/expiry filter (auth.py:357-360), and the sweep deletes only revoked_at IS NOT NULL AND <now-30d (main.py:795-798), so expired-but-unrevoked rows are both listed and never reaped.

### BUG-023 — [P2][correctness] Create-budget modal shows "Budget saved" and keeps the optimistic row even when the server REJECTS the write (409 duplicate-scope / 4xx) — row then silently vanishes on next sync

_budgets · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/helpers.ts:404-417`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:593-596`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:395-419`, `frontend/static/js/src/routes/budgets.py:183-194`
- **Symptom:** When the server rejects a new budget — most reachably a 409 "A budget with this scope already exists" (same trip+category+person already budgeted, e.g. created on another device, or re-creating a just-deleted scope) — the modal still closes, flashes a green "Budget saved." toast, and leaves the new card on screen. The api layer simultaneously fires a confusing "stale edit" toast and a background pullFromServer() that wipes the optimistic row, so the budget the user was just told was "saved" disappears moments later.
- **Root cause:** helpers.ts:408-411 does `await upsertBudget(budget); close(); showLiquidAlert(savedToast)` inside a try/catch. But `upsertBudget` → `_upsertWithUpdatedAt` (api.ts:376) RETURNS a resolved `{ok:false,status:409|4xx}` on any non-2xx (it only throws nothing — even the network catch at api.ts:433 returns `{ok:false}`). So the catch block (helpers.ts:412-417) is dead for server rejections; the success path always runs. The modal never inspects `result.ok`. This is the FE-2 "honest save" pattern that WAS applied to the expense form (ManualTab.tsx:473-474 checks `if (!res || !res.ok)`) but missed for budgets. On 409 the api layer also shows `errors.staleEdit` + calls `pullFromServer()` (api.ts:413-416), producing a double-toast and the vanishing-row desync.
- **Repro:** 1) Two browser sessions for the same user (or one device offline-create then a second create of the same scope after sync). 2) In session A create a budget scoped to Trip X / Food / Everyone; it syncs. 3) In session B (or after deleting+re-creating fast) create a budget with the identical scope. 4) Server returns 409 (scope dup). 5) Modal closes, shows green "Budget saved." AND a "stale edit" toast; the card appears then disappears on the next /api/data poll. User believes a budget was saved that never persisted.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the modal honest like the expense form: `const res = await upsertBudget(budget); if (!res || !res.ok) { rollback STATE.budgets; show res.body?.error || createSaveFailed; keep modal open; return; } close(); showLiquidAlert(savedToast);`. Optionally pre-check for an existing same-scope budget client-side before POSTing to give a friendlier "this scope already has a budget" message.
- **Verifier:** helpers.ts:408-417 awaits upsertBudget then unconditionally close()+saved-toast inside try, but \_upsertWithUpdatedAt (api.ts:417/419/435) RESOLVES {ok:false} on 409/4xx/network-error and never throws, so the catch is dead and the modal never checks result.ok — on a server rejection it falsely reports "saved", keeps the optimistic row, and (on 409) api.ts:413-416 then fires a stale-edit toast + pullFromServer that wipes the row, exactly the honest-save pattern ManualTab.tsx already applies but budgets missed.

### BUG-024 — [P2][bug] Friend-invite strips the new companion's linkedUserId server-side (upsert fires before the member row exists) → 'Pending' badge silently reverts to 'Unlinked' and a duplicate chip appears when they accept

_companions · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.83_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/modals/companions.ts:367-369`, `src/routes/trips.py:42-62`, `src/validators.py:447-449`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:147-150`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:183`, `frontend/static/js/src/main.ts:261-269`
- **Symptom:** Owner adds a friend (or links an existing unlinked companion) to a trip. The picker briefly shows '⏳ Pending'. Within ~15s (the next /api/data poll) the badge reverts to 'Unlinked' on its own. If the friend then accepts the invite, the trip roster shows TWO chips for the same person — one accepted member chip (from trip.members) and one stale 'Unlinked' companion chip — because the companion is no longer linked to their user id.
- **Root cause:** In the friend-add handler the writes run in the order: emit → `void upsertTrip(trip)` (fires POST /api/trips immediately, carrying the companion with the freshly-set `linkedUserId`) → `await inviteTripMember(...)` (creates the `pending` trip_members row). The server's `_cleaned_companions` (trips.py:42-62) builds `verified_linked_ids` = the set of user_ids currently in `trip_members`, and `clean_companions` (validators.py:447-449) coerces any `linkedUserId` NOT in that set to None. Because the upsert reaches SQLite before the invite has created the member row, `friendId` is not yet a member, so the link is stripped and the companion is persisted as name-only. The local STATE keeps the link optimistically, but `pullFromServer` overwrites `trip.companions` wholesale from the server value (`companions: normalizeTripCompanions(t.companions)` at api.ts:149; only the 4 heavy media fields are merged, never companions), so the next 15s poll clobbers the optimistic link with the stripped server copy. Nothing re-links companions from trip_members on read, so once the friend accepts, `buildRosterChips` can't dedupe the companion against the member (the `linkedUserId` is gone) and renders both.
- **Repro:** 1. Owner opens a trip's Companions picker. 2. Click 'Add a friend', pick a friend, choose a role, click '+ Add'. 3. Observe '⏳ Pending' badge. 4. Wait ~15s (one /api/data poll) — badge flips to 'Unlinked'. 5. As the friend, accept the invite. 6. As the owner, reopen the trip — the friend now appears twice (one role-badged member chip + one 'Unlinked' companion chip).
- **Suggested fix:** Reorder so the member row exists before the companion link is persisted: `await inviteTripMember(...)` FIRST, then set `linkedUserId` and call `upsertTrip(trip)`. Alternatively await the upsert AND fire a `pullFromServer()` after the invite so STATE reconciles.
