Best: have the server backfill `companions[].linkedUserId` from accepted/pending trip_members on the read path (data.py member shaping) so a stripped link self-heals regardless of write ordering.
- **Verifier:** companions.ts:368-369 fires `void upsertTrip(trip)` (un-awaited, carries the fresh linkedUserId) BEFORE `await inviteTripMember`; upsert_trip runs \_cleaned_companions (trips.py:254 + 42-62) which strips any linkedUserId not yet in trip_members, the read path (data.py:1055/1121) never re-links companions to members, and pullFromServer overwrites trip.companions wholesale (api.ts:147-149) while buildRosterChips dedupes only on linkedUserId (TripBody.tsx:802) — a genuine race that reverts the link and renders a duplicate chip, but no data loss (name + member row + ghost-roster balances survive), so P2 not P1.

### BUG-025 — [P2][correctness] Invite failures (409 role-conflict, 404 blocked/unknown user, 403) are swallowed: companion is still linked + persisted and a false 'invited' success toast shows

_companions · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/modals/companions.ts:367-372`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/feed.ts:267-274`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:296-300`, `src/routes/trips.py:899-903`, `src/routes/trips.py:869-876`
- **Symptom:** Owner re-adds/links a friend whose invite the server rejects (e.g. the friend is already an accepted member with a different role → 409, or the friend has blocked the owner / is unknown → 404). The picker still attaches the link locally, persists the trip, and shows the green '{name} invited as {role}' toast — even though no invite was created and (for 409) the role was NOT changed. The role badge keeps showing the OLD role on the next poll, contradicting the toast.
- **Root cause:** `inviteTripMember` uses `_post` (api/core.ts:296), which returns the raw Response (or undefined on network error) and never throws. The handler does `await inviteTripMember(trip.id, friendId, role)` (companions.ts:369) but ignores the result entirely, then unconditionally sets the link (lines 353-365), calls upsertTrip, and fires the success toast (line 372). The server returns 409 'Member already accepted with a different role' (trips.py:899-903) and 404 for blocked/nonexistent targets (trips.py:869-876), none of which surface to the user.
- **Repro:** 1. Invite a friend as Relaxer; have them accept. 2. Reopen the picker, 'Add a friend', pick the SAME friend, choose Planner, '+ Add'. 3. Server returns 409 (role unchanged). 4. UI shows '{name} invited as Planner' and a Planner badge momentarily — but the next poll shows them still as Relaxer, with no error.
- **Suggested fix:** Switch `inviteTripMember` to return `{ok,status,body}` (like `_postJson`) and branch on it in the handler: on non-ok, revert the optimistic link, skip the success toast, and show an actionable error (e.g. for 409 surface 'They're already a member as {current_role}; remove then re-invite to change the role'). Only persist + toast on success.
- **Verifier:** inviteTripMember uses \_post (core.ts:296-300) which .catch()es and returns the raw Response without throwing; companions.ts:369 ignores the result, sets the link optimistically + upserts (368), and unconditionally shows the success toast (372), so the server's 409 (trips.py:899-903) and 404 blocked/unknown (trips.py:869-876) never surface.

### BUG-026 — [P2][data-loss] Batch import never persists auto-created categories (syncWithServer is an empty no-op) — imported expenses lose their category on reload

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.93_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:414-419`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:460-464`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:47-81`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:574-589`
- **Symptom:** After a Splitwise/custom-format import that introduces new category names (e.g. 'Transportation', 'Groceries'), the categories appear locally and the imported rows show the right icon — but after the next 15s poll or a page reload they all collapse to the fallback 💰 icon with no category name, and the categories are gone from Settings. The expenses are silently mis-categorized.
- **Root cause:** runBatchImport() pushes newly-inferred categories into STATE.categories (upload.ts:417-419) and at the end calls `void syncWithServer()` (line 463) whose comment claims it 'persists the categories the import created'. But syncWithServer() was gutted: its body is now `JSON.stringify({})` — a connectivity probe that sends NOTHING (api.ts:74-81). Categories now persist ONLY via the per-row delta endpoint syncCategories() (/api/categories), which upload.ts never imports or calls. The per-row upsertExpense writes the expense with a category_id pointing at the new local category, and the server stores that category_id as a free string with no existence check (routes/expenses.py has no FROM categories validation). On the next /api/data pull, STATE.categories is overwritten with the server's set (api.ts:236), which lacks the import-created category, so e.categoryId is now dangling and HistoryTab renders `cat ? cat.icon : '💰'` (HistoryTab.tsx:297,311).
- **Repro:** 1. Create a fresh trip. 2. Expenses → Upload → Batch → Splitwise format. 3. Import a CSV whose Category column has a value not already in your categories (e.g. 'Transportation'). 4. Rows show with an inferred icon and the new category exists. 5. Wait ~15s or reload. 6. The category is gone; every imported row shows 💰 and is uncategorized; Insights category breakdown loses them too.
- **Suggested fix:** In runBatchImport(), replace the trailing `void syncWithServer()` with `void syncCategories()` (import it from ../api.js) so the import-created categories are pushed through the delta endpoint that actually persists them. (Same call Settings/Personalization use after a category edit.)
- **Verifier:** Verified: syncWithServer() POSTs JSON.stringify({}) (api.ts:80, a connectivity probe), upload.ts imports only {syncWithServer, upsertExpense} (line 11) never syncCategories, and the sole state:changed subscriber is saveState→localStorage (state.ts:438), so an import-created STATE.categories row is never sent server-side and is overwritten on the next /api/data pull (api.ts:236) → HistoryTab renders the 💰 fallback (HistoryTab.tsx:311); downgraded from P1 because the expense itself (amount/who/splits/categoryId string) is persisted by upsertExpense — only the category label/grouping is lost, and it's re-creatable.

### BUG-027 — [P2][data-loss] Batch import never persists the companions it auto-adds — imported payers/splitters vanish on reload and become unselectable in the manual form

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:390-398`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:460-464`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:47-81`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:531-540`
- **Symptom:** Importing a Tricount/Splitwise file adds every 'Paid by' name and every split participant to the trip roster (so balances render right immediately), but after the next poll/reload those companions are gone from the trip. The manual 'Who paid' / 'Split between' dropdowns no longer list the imported people, so you can't add a new expense for a payer that the import introduced.
- **Root cause:** runBatchImport() calls addTripCompanion(activeTrip, who) and addTripCompanion for each split name (upload.ts:390-398), which mutates activeTrip.companions in STATE. Companions persist only as part of a trip upsert (upsertTrip → /api/trips), but the import never calls upsertTrip, and the only other persistence channel, syncWithServer(), now sends an empty body (api.ts:74-81). So the roster mutation lives in localStorage/STATE only; the next /api/data pull overwrites STATE.trips with server truth (no imported companions). HistoryTab masks this with a fallback that derives payers from expense `who` values (HistoryTab.tsx:64-74), but ManualTab's 'Who paid' select has NO such fallback (ManualTab.tsx:531-540) — it shows only activeTrip.companions, so after reload the imported payers are unselectable.
- **Repro:** 1. Fresh trip with no companions. 2. Import a Tricount export with payers Alice/Bob. 3. Roster now has Alice/Bob; balances show. 4. Reload. 5. Trip companions list is empty again; manual expense 'Who paid' offers only 'Add companions from Home'; Alice/Bob are gone.
- **Suggested fix:** After the import loop, persist the roster: call upsertTrip(activeTrip) (or the trip-meta upsert) once if any companions were added, in addition to the per-row expense writes. Alternatively, route companion additions through the same persistence the Home CompanionsCard uses.
- **Verifier:** Verified: addTripCompanion mutates trip.companions in place and its docstring says 'caller is responsible for persisting via upsertTrip' (companions.ts:135-155), but runBatchImport/BatchUpload never call upsertTrip and syncWithServer sends nothing, so the next pull overwrites STATE.trips (api.ts:147-184) and ManualTab's 'Who paid' select (no who-fallback, ManualTab.tsx:531-540) can't select the imported payer; downgraded from P1 because expense who/splits are stored on the expense row and balances still compute — only the roster chips/dropdown degrade and are re-addable.

### BUG-028 — [P2][data-loss] Batch import reports 'Imported N' optimistically; rows the server rejects (amount > 1e9, dup cross-trip id, archived, stale) are silently dropped

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:374-385`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:440-447`, `src/validators.py:147-166`, `src/routes/expenses.py:134-145`
- **Symptom:** The import success line ('Imported N') counts rows that the server later refuses. A spreadsheet with, say, a 2,000,000,000 amount, or a row whose generated id happens to collide, reports as imported and shows in the list, then disappears on the next reload with no error shown to the user.
- **Root cause:** runBatchImport increments `added` and pushes to STATE.expenses purely on client-side optimistic success, then fires `void upsertExpense(expense)` (upload.ts:446) WITHOUT awaiting or inspecting the result. The client filter only rejects non-finite/<=0/no-rate values (line 374); it has NO upper bound, while the server's validate_money caps at \_MAX_MONEY = 1e9 (validators.py:162-165) and the route returns 400. Because the POST result is discarded, a 400/403/409 is invisible: the row is counted, shown, and only vanishes when /api/data next overwrites STATE.expenses. (Contrast the manual form, which DOES await upsertExpense and shows 'saveFailed' — upload does not.)
- **Repro:** 1. Build a CSV with one row amount = 5000000000 EUR (and some valid rows). 2. Import. 3. Status says 'Imported N' counting the bad row; it appears in History. 4. Reload. 5. The 5e9 row is gone; no error was ever surfaced.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the import await per-row results (e.g. Promise.allSettled over the upserts) and subtract rejected rows from `added`, surfacing them in the skipped list; and/or mirror the server's 1e9 cap in the client filter alongside the finite/>0 check so over-cap rows are reported as skipped rather than faux-imported.
- **Verifier:** Verified: the client filter (upload.ts:374) only rejects non-finite/<=0/no-rate with no upper bound while the server caps at \_MAX_MONEY=1e9→400 (validators.py:91,162), and runBatchImport does `void upsertExpense(expense)` (line 446) without awaiting/inspecting the result (and a non-2xx HTTP response doesn't even hit the outbox catch in core.ts), so amount>1e9 and archived-trip(409) rows are counted in 'added' yet vanish on the next pull; the 'dup cross-trip id' sub-claim is weak since generateId() ids never collide, but the core over-count is real.

### BUG-029 — [P2][correctness] Popular-format default split is computed against a roster that grows row-by-row, so equal-split percentages depend on import order

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.82_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:390-412`
- **Symptom:** Importing a Tricount/Splitwise file into a trip with no pre-existing companions assigns inconsistent equal-split percentages: the first expense is split among only the people seen so far, later expenses among more people. Two dinners both 'shared by everyone' end up with different debt splits purely because of their position in the file, corrupting the settle-up balances.
- **Root cause:** Inside the per-row loop, addTripCompanion(activeTrip, who) runs first (upload.ts:390-392), then the no-splits default does `const tripRoster = getTripCompanionNames(activeTrip)` and divides 100/tripRoster.length across the CURRENT roster (lines 404-408). Because the roster accumulates as rows are processed, row 1 (only Alice seen) → {Alice:100}; row 2 (Bob now seen) → {Alice:50,Bob:50}; etc. For the canonical 'I have a Tricount, let me import the whole trip' flow the roster starts empty, so early rows are systematically mis-split.
- **Repro:** 1. Fresh trip, no companions. 2. Import a Tricount CSV: row1 Paid by Alice, row2 Paid by Bob, row3 Paid by Carol, none with an explicit splits column. 3. Open settle-up. 4. Row1 is charged 100% to Alice, row2 50/50, row3 33/33/33 — the same 'shared' intent produces three different splits driven by order.
- **Suggested fix:** Two-pass the import: first pass collects all `who`/split names to build the full roster (and register companions), second pass assigns the equal-split default against that complete, order-independent roster. Or default popular-format rows to {who:100} and let the user pick a shared split explicitly.
- **Verifier:** Verified: inside the per-row forEach, addTripCompanion runs first (upload.ts:390-392) then getTripCompanionNames(activeTrip) divides 100/length over the CURRENT accumulated roster (upload.ts:404-408), so early Tricount/Splitwise rows (which carry no splits column) are split across fewer people than later rows → order-dependent, wrong per-person balances; money-affecting so P2 stands.

### BUG-030 — [P2][correctness] Splitwise import hardcodes payer 'Me' and creates a literal 'Me' companion, mislabeling every imported row's payer

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:335-343`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:390-392`
- **Symptom:** Every expense imported via the Splitwise format is attributed to a payer named 'Me', and a companion literally named 'Me' is added to the trip roster. The History payer column and the per-person balances all read 'Me' regardless of who actually paid, and 'Me' shows up as a selectable companion forever.
- **Root cause:** The splitwise branch sets `who = 'Me'` unconditionally (upload.ts:341) because the chosen Splitwise column layout [Date, Description, Category, Cost, Currency] has no payer column. addTripCompanion(activeTrip, 'Me') then plants 'Me' in the roster (line 390-392). Splitwise's real CSV export does contain per-person paid/owed columns, but this mapping ignores them, so the payer attribution is fabricated and balances are wrong whenever the user wasn't the sole payer.
- **Repro:** 1. Expenses → Upload → Batch → Splitwise. 2. Import any Splitwise CSV. 3. Every row's payer is 'Me'; the trip companions list now contains 'Me'; settle-up credits all spend to 'Me'.
- **Suggested fix:** Don't hardcode a 'Me' companion. Either map an actual payer column from the Splitwise export (its full export has paid-by data), or leave `who` empty and prompt the user to assign the payer post-import; at minimum don't inject a literal 'Me' into the roster.
- **Verifier:** Verified: the splitwise branch sets who='Me' unconditionally (upload.ts:341) and addTripCompanion(activeTrip,'Me') plants it (line 390-392); the app's Splitwise layout [Date,Description,Category,Cost,Currency] (BatchUpload POPULAR_SAMPLES) genuinely has no payer column, so payer attribution is fabricated and balances are wrong whenever the user wasn't the sole payer — real correctness bug at P2.

### BUG-031 — [P2][security] Explore feed block filter is one-directional — leaks blocked-by users' public-trip cards into the blocker-target's Explore

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `src/routes/feed.py:456`, `src/routes/public.py:553`, `src/feed_events.py:1112`
- **Symptom:** If B blocks A, B's public trips still appear in A's Explore feed — card shows B's trip name, country, cover photo, owner first-name + avatar, view count, and the share_token. Every other read path (feed actor pool, public profile, public trip, share payload) hides content on a block edge in BOTH directions; Explore does not, so the block is leaky here and the app is internally inconsistent.
- **Root cause:** The explore_feed query only excludes trips owned by users the CALLER has blocked: `AND t.user_id NOT IN (SELECT blocked_id FROM blocks WHERE blocker_id = ?)` (feed.py:456-458). It omits the reverse direction (`SELECT blocker_id FROM blocks WHERE blocked_id = ?`). Compare build_feed_context (feed_events.py:1117-1122) and public.py:553-554, which both filter both directions. The inline comment at feed.py:430 even claims 'block-aware Explore' but only implemented one side.
- **Repro:** 1) User B creates a public+shared trip (so it is Explore-eligible). 2) B blocks A (POST /api/blocks/<A>). 3) A opens the Explore tab. 4) B's trip card still renders with B's name/picture/country/cover and the share token. (Clicking through 404s at /share/<token> since that path checks both directions, so the leak is card-metadata, not full trip.)
- **Suggested fix:** Add the reverse-direction exclusion to the explore query: also `AND t.user_id NOT IN (SELECT blocker_id FROM blocks WHERE blocked_id = ?)`, passing user_id a fourth time. Mirror the bidirectional pattern already used in feed_events.py and public.py.
- **Verifier:** explore_feed (feed.py:456-458) filters only `t.user_id NOT IN (SELECT blocked_id ... blocker_id = ?)` whereas build_feed_context (feed_events.py:1117-1122) and fetch_share_payload (public.py:552-554) both filter BOTH directions, so a user who blocked the caller still has their (deliberately-public) trip cards surface in the caller's Explore, contradicting the inline 'block-aware Explore' claim at feed.py:430.

### BUG-032 — [P2][correctness] Comment count vs. comment list desync after a block (third-party posts)

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/feed.py:181`, `src/routes/feed.py:1135`, `src/routes/blocks.py:148`
- **Symptom:** After A blocks B, a shared trip owned by a THIRD party C (which both A and B commented on) shows a comment chip count that includes B's comment, but expanding the thread shows fewer comments. e.g. the card reads '3 comments' but the thread renders only 2. The count never matches what the user can actually see.
- **Root cause:** `list_feed_comments` filters out blocked authors: `AND c.user_id NOT IN (SELECT blocked_id FROM blocks WHERE blocker_id = ?)` (feed.py:1135-1145). But `_attach_engagement_counts` computes comment_count with a plain `SELECT event_id, COUNT(*) FROM feed_comments ... GROUP BY event_id` (feed.py:181-186) with NO block filter. The block sweep in blocks.py:148-162 only deletes the blocked user's engagement on the BLOCKER'S OWN feed_posts, never on a third party's post, so B's comment on C's share survives and inflates the count for A.
- **Repro:** 1) C shares a public trip. 2) A and B both comment on it. 3) A blocks B. 4) A reloads the feed: the comment chip on C's card counts B's comment, but opening the thread hides it → count > visible rows.
- **Suggested fix:** Apply the same block filter to the count query as to the list: in \_attach_engagement_counts, exclude comments authored by users in `blocked_ids_for(cursor, user_id)` when computing comment_count (and ideally like_count). Or compute counts from the same filtered query the list uses.
- **Verifier:** \_attach_engagement_counts computes comment_count via a plain COUNT(\*) GROUP BY with no block filter (feed.py:181-186) while list_feed_comments DOES exclude blocked authors (feed.py:1141-1143), and the block sweep only deletes engagement on event_ids built from the BLOCKER'S OWN feed_posts (blocks.py:149-162), so a blocked user's comment on a third party's share survives and inflates the count above the rendered list.

### BUG-033 — [P2][data-loss] Deleting a day silently RESURRECTS its pruned photos/documents — server delete_day media cascade undone by the client's loss-free union merge

_itinerary · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.82_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/handlers.ts:272-325`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:107-174`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:40-52`, `src/routes/days.py:264-347`
- **Symptom:** After a planner deletes a numbered day that had photos/documents attached (day-tagged), the server correctly prunes those items and frees their files (delete_day cascade, days.py:264-347). But on the next trip-media write (e.g. adding any photo, toggling the trip checklist), the deleted day's photos/documents reappear on the server — now orphaned with a dangling dayId pointing to a non-existent day — and their files are re-referenced (the earlier disk cleanup is undone). The day's media 'comes back from the dead'.
- **Root cause:** Frontend deleteDay (handlers.ts:272-325) removes the day from STATE.tripDays and calls deleteDayOnServer, but never cleans the local `trip.photos`/`trip.documents`/`trip.markedPlaces` of items tagged with the deleted dayId, and never calls fetchTripMedia. delete_day bumps trips.media_updated_at when it prunes (days.py:338-347), so the client's next persistTripMedia gets a 409. The 409 handler (media.ts:128-159) merges via `_mergeMediaField`, which is a pure UNION by key (media.ts: keeps every server item + adds any LOCAL item missing from the server set). Because the server PRUNED the day-tagged items, they are 'missing' on the server side, so the union RE-ADDS the stale local copies and POSTs them back. The merge has zero deletion/tombstone awareness — the comment at media.ts:163-164 even claims 're-parking ... can't resurrect a peer's delete', which is exactly the wrong assumption: a server-side delete (cascade OR a peer removing a photo) is indistinguishable from 'an item the local side should re-add'.
- **Repro:** 1) Open a trip, attach a photo to Day 3 (via day-tagged Photos). 2) Delete Day 3 from the Path tab. 3) Server prunes the Day-3 photo + deletes its file. 4) Without reloading, add any photo to the Trip Hub (or toggle a checklist item). 5) Re-open the trip / GET /api/trips/<id>/media: the deleted Day-3 photo is back, tagged with the now-dead dayId; its file is referenced again.
- **Suggested fix:** In deleteDay (handlers.ts), before/after deleteDayOnServer, drop local media tied to the deleted dayId: prune `trip.photos`/`trip.documents` items whose dayId === deletedId and NULL the dayId on matching markedPlaces (mirror the server cascade in days.py:264-322), then call persistTripMedia(trip) or fetchTripMedia(trip.id) so local and server agree. Longer-term: give the media merge deletion awareness (tombstones or a server-authoritative removal set) so union-merge can't resurrect any server-side delete.
- **Verifier:** deleteDay (handlers.ts:289-322) filters STATE.tripDays but never prunes trip.photos/documents/markedPlaces of the deleted dayId nor calls fetchTripMedia, and \_mergeMediaField (media.ts:62-73) is a pure union with zero tombstone awareness, so a media write after the delete re-POSTs the still-local pruned items back over the server's cascade — but it's conditional (a plain fetchTripMedia with no parked write OVERWRITES local arrays at media.ts:231-234 and self-heals, and the resurrected items are the user's own bytes, not a true loss), so P2 not P1.

### BUG-034 — [P2][correctness] Parallel renumber upserts collide on UNIQUE(trip_id, day_number) after deleting a middle day → numbering gap + spurious 'another device updated this day' toast

_itinerary · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.72_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/handlers.ts:296-320`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/trip.ts:609-622`, `frontend/static/js/src/api.ts:453-462`, `migrations/versions/c9d0e1f2a3b4_trip_days_unique_excludes_tombstones.py`
- **Symptom:** Deleting a middle day on a multi-day trip can leave a numbering gap (e.g. delete Day 2 of 1..5 and end up with 1,2,4 or a missing number) and pop a misleading 'Stale edit — another device updated this day' toast even when the user is the only editor. The state self-heals only on next page load (normalizeDayNumbers boot self-heal).
- **Root cause:** deleteDay renumbers survivors in memory to a contiguous 1..N (handlers.ts:296-301) then persists them with `Promise.all(...map(upsertDay))` (handlers.ts:318-320) — UNORDERED parallel writes. The same pattern is in the edit-dates finalize (trip.ts:621). When numbers shift DOWNWARD into still-occupied slots, two parallel upserts race against the partial UNIQUE index idx_trip_days_trip_day_number(trip_id, day_number) WHERE deleted_at IS NULL. Example: survivors [d3→2, d4→3, d5→4]; if upsertDay(d5→4) executes before upsertDay(d4→3) commits, d5's target 4 still collides with d4's live row (number 4) → IntegrityError → days.py:161-181 returns 409. The client's 409 handler (api.ts:453-462) shows the stale-edit toast + pullFromServer but does NOT retry with a corrected number, so the survivor keeps its old number and a gap persists until reload.
- **Repro:** Create a 5-day trip (Days 1..5). Delete Day 2. Intermittently (race-dependent) one survivor's upsert returns 409: a stale-edit toast appears and the day chips show a gap/duplicate; reloading the page silently repairs it via normalizeDayNumbers.
- **Suggested fix:** Persist the renumbered survivors SEQUENTIALLY in an order that never collides — e.g. when numbers decrease, write in ascending target order; when they increase, descending — or write them in two phases (park to a temporary high range, then to final). Alternatively, add a server-side batch-renumber endpoint that updates all day_numbers in one transaction. At minimum, treat a 409 during a renumber as 'retry with fresh state' rather than surfacing a stale-edit toast.
- **Verifier:** handlers.ts:296-320 renumbers survivors to 1..N then fires `Promise.all(...map(upsertDay))` (unordered), the partial UNIQUE idx_trip_days_trip_day_number(trip_id,day_number) WHERE deleted_at IS NULL exists (migration c9d0e1f2a3b4), and a downward-shift upsert can hit an as-yet-unrenumbered live row → IntegrityError → days.py:177-180 returns 409 → api.ts:453-462 only toasts+pullFromServer with NO corrected-number retry, leaving a gap until reload.

### BUG-035 — [P2][bug] EXIF-tagged photos render TWICE in the PDF: once in the day card, once in the trip-wide Photos gallery

_journey-media-pdf · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:1066-1089`, `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:530-534`, `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:886-908`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/tripMediaModals.ts:416-432`
- **Symptom:** When a user exports a trip PDF with both the Day-by-day section and Photos enabled, every photo that was auto-tagged to a content day (the common case) appears twice in the document — embedded in that day's thumbnail grid AND again in the dedicated trip-wide Photos gallery. The PDF is visibly padded with duplicate images and extra pages, and a 60-photo trip can double its gallery-section weight.
- **Root cause:** The route merges trip-level photos_json entries that carry a `dayId` into that day's `photos` column so the day card embeds them (**init**.py:1076-1089), then renders the day card via `_collect_photos(day['photos'])` (line 533). Separately, the trip-wide gallery calls `_collect_photos(trip_photos, limit=_PHOTO_MAX_PER_TRIP)` over the FULL, UNFILTERED `photos_json` list (line 893; `trip_photos = _safe_json(trip_row.get('photos_json'), [])` at line 251). The gallery never excludes the day-tagged photos already inlined into day cards. The docstring at line 887-888 explicitly claims the gallery shows 'any per-day photos not already inlined in the day cards', but the code does no such filtering, and `_collect_photos`/`_photo_grid` perform no dedup. Photos are routinely day-tagged because the Photos-tab upload path EXIF-matches each file to a day and calls `addTripPhoto(trip, { src, dayId })` (tripMediaModals.ts:425-429).
- **Repro:** 1. Open a trip, go to the Photos tab, upload several phone photos whose EXIF capture dates fall within the trip's day range (they auto-tag to those days). 2. Export PDF with both 'Day plan' and 'Photos' checked. 3. Observe each tagged photo appears in its day's card AND again in the Photos section. (Tests miss this: test_pdf4_photos_section_appears_when_toggled at tests/test_pdf_mk4.py:206 uses a trip-level photo with NO dayId plus a separate legacy day.photos string, so the dayId-tagged double-embed path is never exercised.)
- **Suggested fix:** In the gallery branch (around **init**.py:892-893), build the gallery from only the trip photos with NO dayId (or whose dayId is not a renderable day), e.g. `gallery_entries = [p for p in trip_photos if not (isinstance(p, dict) and p.get('dayId') in renderable_day_ids)]` then `_collect_photos(gallery_entries, ...)`. Photos tagged to Day 0 / a non-rendered day should still fall through to the gallery so they aren't lost.

### BUG-036 — [P2][correctness] Uploaded documents (boarding passes / bookings) are never included in the exported PDF and have no export toggle

_journey-media-pdf · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:111-961`, `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:1011-1019`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/pdf.ts:62-87`, `src/routes/pdf/_i18n.py:34-43`
- **Symptom:** A user uploads trip documents (PDF tickets, hotel bookings, boarding passes) via the Documents tab, then exports the trip PDF expecting a printable record. The documents are completely absent: there is no Documents section, no list of document names/links, and the export modal offers no 'Documents' option at all. The data is silently omitted with zero indication.
- **Root cause:** The PDF builder `_build_trip_pdf` has sections for days, to-dos, budgets, expenses, settlements, companions, marked places, and photos — but NONE for documents. The export route's trip SELECT (`__init__.py:1014-1016`) never fetches `documents_json`, and `trip.documents` / day `tickets` are never read in the builder. The i18n string table (`_i18n.py`) has no `sec_documents` key. The export modal (`modals/pdf.ts:62-87`) renders an `includePhotos` checkbox but no documents checkbox. So documents — a first-class media type with their own write path and Documents UI tab — are structurally unrepresented in the export.
- **Repro:** 1. Open a trip, Documents tab, upload a PDF ticket (trip-wide or attached to a day). 2. Export the trip PDF with all options checked. 3. The resulting PDF contains no reference to the uploaded document anywhere.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an `includeDocuments` section: fetch `documents_json` in the route SELECT, merge day-level `tickets` like photos, and render a 'Documents' section listing each document's name + URL (documents are arbitrary files — link/list them rather than embedding). Add a `sec_documents` i18n key across all four locales and an `includeDocuments` checkbox in modals/pdf.ts. At minimum, list document names so the user knows what is attached.

### BUG-037 — [P2][correctness] Cloned trip's cover image breaks when the source owner revokes the share or deletes the trip

_journey-share-clone · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.74_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:1319`, `src/main.py:1448`, `src/main.py:1326`, `src/routes/trips.py:347`
- **Symptom:** A stranger clones a trip; the clone's cover photo renders fine at first, then later turns into a broken image. The cloner "owns" the trip but cannot load its cover. If the original owner deletes the source trip entirely, the cover 404s permanently with no recovery.
- **Root cause:** `_clone_trip_attempt` copies the SOURCE owner's `cover_url` verbatim (trips.py:1319), e.g. `/static/uploads/<ownerA>/abc.jpg`. The clone row is private: `is_archived=0, is_public=0`, no share_token. The serve_upload gate (main.py:1294) can't authorize the cloner: the owner-dir fast-path fails (file is in ownerA's dir, not the cloner's, main.py:1326), and the member-join requires BOTH the caller and the file's owner to be accepted members of a trip referencing the file (main.py:1364-1378) — but ownerA is not a member of the clone, and the cloner is not a member of the source. The only thing keeping the cover visible is the anonymous public-cover fallback (main.py:1448-1456), which matches `cover_url` only on trips where `is_public=1 OR share_token IS NOT NULL`. That row is the SOURCE trip. So the clone's cover lives or dies by the source's share/public state: revoke the share link (revoke_share_link sets share_token=NULL, trips.py:1233) or unpublish, and the clone's cover stops resolving. Delete the source trip and delete_upload_files removes the physical file (trips.py:347/455), 404ing it forever.
- **Repro:** 1. User A creates a trip with an uploaded cover, NOT public, shares via link. 2. Stranger B clones it; B's clone cover renders (served via the share_token public-cover fallback). 3. A opens Share → Unshare (revokes the token). 4. B reloads their cloned trip → cover is now a broken image (clone is private, source no longer public/shared, B isn't a co-member). 5. Alternatively A deletes the source trip → B's cover 404s permanently.
- **Suggested fix:** On clone, copy the cover bytes into the cloner's own upload namespace (/static/uploads/<clonerId>/...) and point the clone's cover_url at that copy, so the clone is self-contained and the owner-dir fast-path authorizes it. At minimum, document/accept that cloned covers are ephemeral, or drop the cover on clone when it's an uploaded file the cloner can't durably access.
- **Verifier:** Clone copies the source owner's cover_url verbatim into a private row (is_public=0 hardcoded, no share_token; trips.py:1293,1319), so serve_upload's owner fast-path and the both-members JSON join both fail for the cloner (main.py:1327,1364-1378) and the cover survives only via the anonymous public-cover fallback that matches the SOURCE trip on is_public=1 OR share_token IS NOT NULL (main.py:1448-1456) — so revoke_share_link (share_token=NULL, trips.py:1233) or delete_trip (collect_trip_upload_paths includes the cover helpers.py:78-80, delete_upload_files rms it trips.py:455) 404s the clone's cover.

### BUG-038 — [P2][correctness] POI 'always anchor' categories (Medical/Pets/Schools/Sports/Transit/Traffic) ignore useAnchorAlways at runtime — pins follow the day pin and Settings lies

_maps · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:410`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/poiCategories.ts:143`, `frontend/static/js/src/state.ts:94`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:596`
- **Symptom:** For a user who has never opened Settings (default poiAnchoring = {}), the six pills declared useAnchorAlways:true do NOT stay anchored to the Trip Hub. When the user selects a numbered day on the wheel, these pills re-fetch and their markers jump to the selected day's pin instead of covering the whole trip — and they fire an extra Places API call on every day change. Settings → General shows these pills as 'Anchor (trip-wide)', so the displayed setting contradicts the actual map behavior.
- **Root cause:** shouldForceAnchor() reads ONLY STATE.preferences?.poiAnchoring?.[cat.key] === 'anchor' and never falls back to cat.useAnchorAlways. The documented contract (state.ts:94-99 and types.d.ts:634-636: 'Empty / missing keys fall back to the category's useAnchorAlways flag') was lost in the React migration — the comment still points at the old pages/home.js. Because the default is {}, shouldForceAnchor returns false for all six categories, so (a) resolveSearchCenter uses the selected day instead of the anchor, and (b) the onSelectedDayChange skip-guard at HeroMap.tsx:624 (`if (cat && shouldForceAnchor(cat)) return;`) never triggers, so they needlessly re-fetch on day change. Settings.tsx:596-601 computes effectiveAnchor WITH the useAnchorAlways fallback, so the UI and the runtime disagree.
- **Repro:** 1. New/default user (never touched Settings → POI). 2. Open a multi-day trip with day pins in different neighborhoods. 3. Turn on the Medical pill while the Hub is selected — hospitals across the trip appear. 4. Select Day 3 on the wheel. Observe Medical markers re-fetch and recenter on Day 3's pin (and an extra Places call fires). 5. Open Settings → General → POI: Medical is shown as Anchor. The map behavior contradicts it.
- **Suggested fix:** In shouldForceAnchor, honor the documented fallback: `const pref = STATE.preferences?.poiAnchoring?.[cat.key]; return pref === 'anchor' || (pref !== 'epicenter' && !!cat.useAnchorAlways);`. This restores the pre-migration contract and the consistency with Settings.tsx's effectiveAnchor.
- **Verifier:** HeroMap.tsx:410-413 shouldForceAnchor returns ONLY STATE.preferences?.poiAnchoring?.[cat.key]==='anchor' with no cat.useAnchorAlways fallback; default poiAnchoring is {} so for the 6 useAnchorAlways:true pills (poiCategories.ts:147-164) it returns false, while Settings.tsx:596-602 applies the fallback — runtime and the documented contract (state.ts:97, types.d.ts:636) genuinely disagree.

### BUG-039 — [P2][correctness] Adding/removing a place to the to-do list from a map InfoWindow does not repaint to-do markers — map diverges from saved state until remount

_maps · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.82_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:320`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:652`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/todoMarkers.ts:70`
- **Symptom:** User clicks a POI pin (or a free-form search hit), then 'Add to to-do list'. The button correctly flips to '✓ On your to-do list' and the data is persisted, but the purple to-do checkmark marker does NOT appear on the map. Conversely, clicking '✓ On your to-do list' to remove leaves the stale to-do marker on the map. The map view silently disagrees with what was saved until the user navigates away and back (or changes the selected day).
- **Root cause:** The InfoWindow toggle handler (wireInfoWindowMarkButtons.todoBtn.onclick, HeroMap.tsx:320-331) calls toggleTodoListMembership + emit('state:changed') + upsertTrip + refresh() but never calls repaintTodoMarkers(). HeroMap's map-setup useEffect depends only on [mapRetryTick], so emit('state:changed') re-renders React but does NOT re-run the effect, so no marker repaint happens. repaintTodoMarkers() is only invoked on initial mount (line 662) and inside onSelectedDayChange (line 620).
- **Repro:** 1. Open a trip on Home with the map. 2. Turn on the Restaurants pill, click a restaurant marker, click 'Add to to-do list'. 3. Button shows '✓ On your to-do list' but no purple to-do square appears at that spot. 4. Switch the wheel to another day and back (or reload) — now the to-do marker appears. Removal has the mirror bug: the to-do marker lingers after removal until a remount.
- **Suggested fix:** Call repaintTodoMarkers() inside the todoBtn.onclick handler after toggleTodoListMembership (right where emit/upsert happen), so the freshly added/removed to-do marker reflects immediately. repaintTodoMarkers is already in scope in the effect closure that builds wireInfoWindowMarkButtons.
- **Verifier:** todoBtn.onclick (HeroMap.tsx:320-331) calls refresh() which (314-319) only does iw.setContent + re-wire, never repaintTodoMarkers(); the effect deps are [mapRetryTick] (line 873) so emit('state:changed') re-renders React but does not re-run map setup, and repaintTodoMarkers is invoked only at mount (662) and onSelectedDayChange (620).

### BUG-040 — [P2][data-loss] Warm-409 union-merge resurrects a media item the user just deleted (photo / document / checklist to-do / saved place)

_media · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:62`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:107`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:139`, `src/routes/trips.py:786`
- **Symptom:** User A deletes a photo (or a checklist to-do, a saved place, a document). A peer (device B / second tab) made ANY concurrent media change to the same trip. A's delete is silently UNDONE: the deleted item reappears in A's list and is re-persisted to the server. No toast, no indication. This is the same intent-violating, hand-built-list-corruption class as the R12 'Accept Plan deleted my to-dos' P0.
- **Root cause:** `_mergeMediaField(serverItems, pendingItems)` (media.ts:62) builds `out = [...serverItems]` then appends only local items whose key is NOT already on the server. On a warm write, `persistTripMedia` → `_postTripMedia` sends the FULL post-delete snapshot; the server returns 409 with `current` = live media that STILL CONTAINS the deleted item (because the peer's write didn't delete it). The merge keys by stable `id`, sees the deleted item's id present in `cur`, keeps the server copy, and the local snapshot (which OMITS it = the delete) loses. The merged result is reflected into STATE (media.ts:149-158) and retried, persisting the resurrected item. The code comment at media.ts:42-46 asserts union-by-key 'can't resurrect a peer device's delete' and is only sound for the cold-window ADD-only case — but `_postTripMedia`'s 409 loop runs for EVERY warm write, including deletes, where the assumption is false.
- **Repro:** 1. Open the same trip on two devices/tabs (both hydrate media; both hold \_mediaVersion=V0). 2. Device B adds a photo (or toggles any checklist item) → server media=V1, still contains item X. 3. Device A deletes item X (removeTripPhoto/checklist filter → upsertTrip → persistTripMedia, sends snapshot without X, clientMediaUpdatedAt=V0). 4. Server 409s (V0≠V1), echoes current containing X. 5. A's \_mergeMediaField puts X back; retry succeeds. 6. X is alive again on the server and in A's UI — A's delete was silently reverted.
- **Suggested fix:** The union-by-key merge is only correct for adds. For a loss-free 3-way merge of deletes/edits the media items need a soft-delete tombstone (e.g. a deletedAt per item, or send the set of locally-deleted ids in the 409 retry so the merge can subtract them) — mirroring how expenses/days/budgets use deleted_at tombstones. At minimum, compute the local delete-set = (server keys) − (snapshot keys present-before-this-write) and remove those from the merged result; and surface a 'someone else edited this trip' toast on the media 409 instead of silently merging.
- **Verifier:** Verified \_mergeMediaField (media.ts:62-72) seeds out=[...serverItems] and only appends local-only keys, so on a real 409 where cur (media.py:806-811) still contains the item a peer didn't delete, the deleted item survives, is reflected into STATE (media.ts:151-158) and re-POSTed; but unlike the rootCause's 'every warm write' framing the 409 only fires on a genuine concurrent peer media write (stale clientMediaUpdatedAt, trips.py:778-786), so it is a narrow concurrent-delete loss, not an every-delete one -> P2 not P1.

### BUG-041 — [P2][data-loss] Warm-409 union-merge silently discards a concurrent EDIT to an existing media item (checklist toggle, doc rename, photo day-reassign, place forManual/forAI toggle)

_media · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.83_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:62`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/media.ts:139`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/tripMediaModals.ts:678`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/tripChecklistModal.ts:53`
- **Symptom:** User A edits an EXISTING item (e.g. ticks a checklist task done, renames a doc, drags a photo to another day). A peer made any concurrent media change. A's edit is silently reverted to the server's pre-edit value of that item — the modal even repaints to the reverted state on the next poll. The user believes they checked the box / renamed the file, but it didn't stick.
- **Root cause:** Same `_mergeMediaField` (media.ts:62): for an item key present on BOTH sides (the edited item retains its `id`), the server's copy is taken (`out = [...serverItems]`) and the local edited copy is dropped because its key is already `seen`. So 'server wins ties' silently overwrites the local field-level edit. Edits route through `upsertTrip` → `persistTripMedia` → `_postTripMedia`, hitting the same 409 merge. Reorder (tripMediaModals.ts:658-661) is also lost — server item order comes back first, the local reordered array is discarded.
- **Repro:** 1. Two tabs on the same trip, media hydrated. 2. Tab B adds any media item → server version bumps. 3. Tab A toggles checklist item Z's done=true (persist → 409). 4. Merge takes server's Z (done=false) since Z's id is already in the server set; A's done=true is dropped. 5. Z shows unchecked again after the merge/next poll.
- **Suggested fix:** Tie-resolution must not be unconditional server-wins. Use per-item version/last-write-wins-by-timestamp, or send a field-level patch instead of a whole-array snapshot, or (consistent with the rest of the app) give media items an updated_at and merge per item. Also add the media-409 'someone else edited' toast so a dropped edit is at least visible.
- **Verifier:** For an item present on both sides by stable id, \_mergeMediaField starts from the server copy and skips the local edit (its key is already in `seen`), so a field-level edit or reorder is dropped on a 409; edits do route here via upsertTrip->persistTripMedia->\_postTripMedia (api.ts:499; tripChecklistModal.ts:53; tripMediaModals.ts:661/678/886/955), but again only a real concurrent peer media write triggers the 409, making this a narrow concurrency loss -> P2.

### BUG-042 — [P2][bug] HEIC→JPEG re-encode exception fallback writes raw HEIC bytes into a .jpg file → broken image served as image/jpeg

_media · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `src/routes/media.py:232`, `src/routes/media.py:295`, `src/routes/media.py:313`
- **Symptom:** An iPhone HEIC upload can land on disk as a file named `*.jpg` whose bytes are actually HEIC. `serve_upload` → `send_from_directory` infers Content-Type from the `.jpg` extension and serves `image/jpeg`, so browsers/lightbox/PDF builder that can't decode HEIC show a broken image — the exact compatibility failure MED-5 set out to fix, reopened on the error path.
- **Root cause:** For `.heic`/`.heif`, `filename`/`out_path` are rewritten to `.jpg` at media.py:232-233 BEFORE the encode. The encode `img.save(out_path, format='JPEG', exif=b'')` (media.py:295) can raise — most realistically `OSError: cannot write mode RGBA/P/LA as JPEG` because there is no `img.convert('RGB')` before the JPEG save — and the broad `except Exception:` at media.py:313-315 then does `file.save(out_path)`, persisting the ORIGINAL HEIC bytes under the `.jpg` name. The happy-path fix (rewriting the extension) made the fallback worse, because the fallback no longer matches the file's true format.
- **Repro:** Upload a HEIC whose decoded image has an alpha/palette mode (or otherwise trips the JPEG encoder, or any decode-OK/encode-fail HEIC). The file saves as `<ts>_<salt>_name.jpg` with HEIC bytes; opening its /static/uploads URL yields a broken image in Chrome/Firefox.
- **Suggested fix:** Before the JPEG save, normalize mode: `if img.mode not in ('RGB','L'): img = img.convert('RGB')`. And in the `except Exception` fallback, if `ext in {'.heic','.heif'}`, do NOT save raw bytes under `.jpg` — either reject with the existing 415 'switch to JPEG' message or save under the original `.heic` extension so Content-Type matches the bytes.
- **Verifier:** Confirmed filename/out_path are rewritten to .jpg at media.py:232-233 before the encode, there is no img.convert('RGB') before img.save(..., format='JPEG') at media.py:295 (so an RGBA/P-mode HEIC raises OSError), and the broad except at media.py:313-315 does file.save(out_path) writing original HEIC bytes under the .jpg name -> serve_upload infers image/jpeg from the extension; real but only for the alpha/palette HEIC subset, so P2 holds.

### BUG-043 — [P2][data-loss] Editing a foreign-currency settlement (name-only companions) silently re-denominates it to the home currency, corrupting the per-currency Settle view

_money-invariant · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.83_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:461`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:462`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:486`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:487`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:253`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:270`
- **Symptom:** A user settles a debt in a foreign currency (e.g. 5000 JPY) between two name-only companions — this takes PATH B and is stored as an isSettlement expense with currency='JPY', value=5000. Later they tap Edit on that settlement. The modal hardcodes the amount field to the HOME-currency conversion of euroValue and, on save, overwrites s.currency=home and s.value=<home amount>. The original JPY settlement is gone: the per-currency Settle view (computeTripBalancesByCurrency, which buckets on raw value+currency) now shows the JPY debt as UNSETTLED again, while a phantom home-currency credit appears in the home-currency bucket. The user thinks they just edited a number; they actually moved the payment to a different currency ledger.
- **Root cause:** openEditSettlementModal's legacy-expense branch is hard-coded to the home currency: the amount input value is convertCurrency(s.euroValue, 'EUR', home) (line 462) and the submit handler sets `s.currency = home` and `s.euroValue = convertCurrency(amount, home, 'EUR')` (lines 486-487), with no currency selector. The original row's currency is discarded. computeTripBalancesByCurrency (balances.ts:253-269) keys strictly on exp.currency+value, so changing the currency moves the settlement to a different per-currency bucket and the original debt re-opens. The server-settlement edit path (openEditServerSettlementModal) correctly preserves `cur = s.currency` (line 534) — only the legacy expense path regresses.
- **Repro:** 1) Trip with two name-only (unlinked) companions and a JPY expense. 2) Settle the JPY debt via the manual settle modal in JPY → stored as isSettlement expense (currency JPY). 3) Open Settle → History → Edit on that settlement, change nothing (or just the people), Save. 4) Go back to the Settle tab: the JPY debt is suggested again as outstanding, and a home-currency entry is now skewed.
- **Suggested fix:** In openEditSettlementModal's legacy-expense branch, add a currency selector (default = s.currency) exactly like openManualSettleModal, pre-fill the amount with the ORIGINAL value in the original currency (not the home conversion), and on save set s.currency to the chosen currency and recompute euroValue via convertCurrency(amount, chosenCur, 'EUR'). Do not force home currency.
- **Verifier:** The legacy isSettlement edit modal (actions.ts:454-470) has NO currency selector and the submit hard-sets s.currency = home + s.euroValue = convertCurrency(amount, home, 'EUR') (486-487) where amount = convertCurrency(s.euroValue,'EUR',home) (462); since computeTripBalancesByCurrency buckets strictly on exp.currency (balances.ts:254) and these foreign legacy rows are creatable via the per-currency manual-settle dropdown (actions.ts:347,371→settleDebt PATH B:206), the edited row jumps currency buckets and re-opens the original-currency debt — but the EUR euroValue round-trips intact (headline EUR balance unaffected), so the blast radius is the per-currency view only, narrower than P1.

### BUG-044 — [P2][correctness] Budget stored in a non-EUR currency (via API/legacy) is read as EUR everywhere, producing wrong spent-vs-target status and Insights totals

_money-invariant · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.74_

- **Files:** `src/routes/budgets.py:48`, `src/routes/budgets.py:49`, `src/routes/budgets.py:203`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/helpers.ts:196`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/helpers.ts:199`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/Budgets.tsx:352`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/insights/Insights.tsx:480`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/insights/Insights.tsx:481`
- **Symptom:** A budget whose stored `currency` is not EUR and whose `amount` is in that foreign currency (the only writer that can do this is the raw /api/budgets POST or legacy data — the in-app create modal always converts to EUR and stamps currency='EUR') is compared against spend that is summed in EUR. The 'spent vs target' percentage, the over/near/ok color tier, and the Insights budget bars are all computed as spent(EUR) / amount(foreign). A 500000 JPY budget (~€3000) is read as a €500000 target, so it renders permanently 'within budget'; conversely a small foreign target reads as wildly over.
- **Root cause:** budgets.py validates and persists `currency` + `amount` verbatim (lines 48-49, INSERT line 203) and there is NO normalization to EUR on the server. Every reader, however, assumes amount is EUR: budgetStatus uses `target = budget.amount` while `spent = Σ euroValue` (helpers.ts:196-199); Budgets.tsx renders `formatHome(b.amount, 'EUR')` (line 352); Insights does `convertCurrency(stat.target, 'EUR', targetCurr)` and `convertCurrency(stat.spent, 'EUR', targetCurr)` (Insights.tsx:480-481). budget.currency is read only for the cosmetic 'was X' suffix, never for the math. The expense write path keeps original currency + a real euro_value, but the budget path has no euro_value column and silently treats amount as EUR.
- **Repro:** POST /api/budgets with {budget:{id, amount: 500000, currency:'JPY', tripId:'all'}} (passes the IA-10 gate because JPY has a live rate). It appears on the Budgets page with target '€500,000' and status OK regardless of real spend; the Insights budget bar uses 500000 as the EUR denominator.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the budget amount canonical EUR on the server (mirror compute_euro_value for expenses): store an euro_value/amount-in-EUR derived from amount+currency at write time, and have all readers compare spent(EUR) against that. Alternatively, have budgetStatus/Insights convert budget.amount from budget.currency to EUR before comparing, instead of assuming EUR.
- **Verifier:** budgets.py validates+persists amount and currency verbatim with no euro_value column and no conversion (INSERT 203-225), and the IA-10 gate (64) only rejects no-rate non-EUR currencies without normalizing them; every reader treats amount as EUR (helpers.ts:198 target=budget.amount vs spent=Σ euroValue; Budgets.tsx:352 formatHome(b.amount,'EUR'); Insights.tsx:480-481 convertCurrency(stat.spent/target,'EUR',targetCurr)), so a rate-backed non-EUR budget posted via raw API/CSV mis-reads — correctness only, and unreachable from the UI which always converts to EUR + sets currency:'EUR' (helpers.ts:388-403).

### BUG-045 — [P2][correctness] Settling the exact foreign-currency debt clears the per-currency Settle view but leaves a residual in the EUR balance / Global tab / Insights (settle-time FX vs frozen expense FX)

_money-invariant · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.68_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/actions.ts:115`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:183`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:92`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:255`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/SettlementView.tsx:175`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/SettlementView.tsx:178`
- **Symptom:** On a trip with a foreign-currency expense entered weeks earlier, a user opens Settle Up, taps the suggested per-currency debt (e.g. 'Sara owes 5000 JPY'), and records it. The per-currency suggestion disappears ('all settled'), but the per-person EUR balance HEADLINE on the same page, the Global cross-trip tab, and the Insights balances still show a small residual debt or credit between the two people that never goes away. The user sees the trip as both settled (suggestions) and unsettled (headline/global) at once.
- **Root cause:** The suggested debts come from computeTripBalancesByCurrency, which nets the expense's RAW `value` in its own currency (balances.ts:255) and subtracts the settlement's raw `amount` — so settling the exact foreign amount zeroes that bucket. But the EUR balance headline (SettlementView.tsx:175 → computeTripBalances) and the Global/Insights views net the expense's euro_value FROZEN at the expense's write-time rate (balances.ts:183), while the settlement contributes settlement.euroValue (balances.ts:92) computed at settle-time via convertCurrency(amount, currency, 'EUR') (actions.ts:115). When the FX rate moved between expense entry and settlement, frozen-euro_value(expense) != settle-time-euro_value(settlement), so the EUR net does not reach zero even though the foreign amounts match exactly. The two coexisting balance models (raw-currency vs frozen-EUR) disagree by the FX drift.
- **Repro:** 1) Enter a 5000 JPY expense split 50/50 (rate frozen, say €31). 2) Wait for/seed a JPY rate change (or set the live rate so today's 5000 JPY = €34). 3) Settle Up → tap the suggested 'X owes 2500 JPY' (records euroValue at €17 today). 4) Per-currency suggestions clear; the EUR balance headline + Global tab still show ~€1.5 owed between the two, indefinitely.
- **Suggested fix:** Pick ONE source of truth for the displayed 'settled?' state. Either (a) drive the per-person headline + Global + Insights from the per-currency netting too (so 'settled' is consistent across views), or (b) when recording a per-currency settlement, snapshot the same write-time euro rate the underlying debt used rather than today's convertCurrency, or (c) absorb sub-threshold FX residue in the EUR view's simplifyDebts epsilon scaled to the trip's FX exposure. At minimum document that the EUR headline can show FX residue after a per-currency settle.
- **Verifier:** The per-currency view nets raw exp.value minus raw s.amount (balances.ts:255,272) so matching foreign amounts zero the bucket, while computeTripBalances nets frozen exp.euroValue (183) against settlement euroValue computed at settle-time (applySettlementToBalances:92; client actions.ts:115 / server settlements.py:211 compute_euro_value both at the live settle-time rate) — so under FX drift the EUR headline + Global + Insights retain a residual; this is a real divergence between the two coexisting balance models, though it is the inherent consequence of the owner-confirmed NOMINAL/write-time-frozen design (money_fx_inflation_invariant.md), not a logic error.

### BUG-046 — [P2][bug] Account deletion / factory-reset fails to clean orphaned engagement notifications (wrong type names + wrong key column)

_notifications · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.92_

- **Files:** `src/routes/data.py:1416-1436`, `src/routes/feed.py:806-808`, `src/routes/trips.py:417-422`
- **Symptom:** After user A deletes their account, share_liked/share_commented/share_reposted notifications that A's posts (especially A's reposts of B's originals) generated on OTHER users' bells survive as orphans. Clicking one routes the recipient to FEED with highlightPostId pointing at a now-deleted post (notifications.ts:344-349), landing on nothing.
- **Root cause:** The factory-reset sweep at data.py:1430-1436 deletes engagement-notification orphans with `... AND type IN ('feed_liked','feed_commented','feed_reposted','feed_bookmarked')` and matches on `related_id IN (doomed_post_ids)`. BOTH are wrong: (1) those four type strings do not exist anywhere in the codebase — the real engagement notification types are 'share_liked'/'share_commented'/'share_reposted' (feed.py:122-129); (2) engagement notifications store the POST in the `post_id` column and the ACTOR's user_id in `related_id` (feed.py:133-135), so filtering by related_id can never match a post id. Net: the DELETE matches zero rows. The single-post delete (feed.py:806) and trip delete (trips.py:420) do it correctly with `DELETE FROM notifications WHERE post_id IN (...)`; the bulk reset path is the broken sibling — the very orphan class the migration f5a6b7c8d9e0 (NF3) added post_id to fix.
- **Repro:** 1. User B shares a public trip (feed_post). 2. User A reposts B's post (fires share_reposted to B, post_id = A's repost id, recipient B). 3. A goes to Profile → delete account / factory reset (/api/data DELETE). 4. A's repost feed_post row is deleted (data.py:1441) but B's share_reposted notification (post_id = A's deleted repost) is NOT deleted (the sweep's type+column filter never matches). 5. B opens the bell, clicks the 'A reposted your share' row → navigates to FEED?highlightPostId=<dead id> → highlights/scrolls to nothing.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace the broken sweep with the same shape the post/trip delete paths use: `DELETE FROM notifications WHERE post_id IN (<doomed_post_ids>)` (drop the bogus type filter and the related_id column). Keep the existing user_id and related_id-by-user sweeps for the user-keyed types.
- **Verifier:** data.py:1432-1436 deletes with `type IN ('feed_liked','feed_commented','feed_reposted','feed_bookmarked')` AND `related_id IN (doomed_post_ids)`, but the only real engagement types are 'share_liked/commented/reposted' (feed.py:122-129) and they store the post in `post_id` with the actor in `related_id` (feed.py:133-135) — so the DELETE matches zero rows while the sibling paths (feed.py:806, trips.py:420) correctly use `WHERE post_id IN (...)`; downgraded to P2 because the frontend now falls back to FEED for a missing postId (notifications.ts:344-349) so the orphans clutter rather than hard-404.

### BUG-047 — [P2][bug] Trip-invite notification is never cleared after Accept/Decline — bell badge stuck unread forever, re-click errors

_notifications · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/notifications.ts:283-290`, `frontend/static/js/src/modals/share.ts:52-83`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/feed.ts:279-285`, `src/routes/trips.py:962-1059`
- **Symptom:** A user taps a 'X invited you to Trip Y' notification, accepts (or declines) in the modal, and the trip_invite notification stays UNREAD in their bell permanently. The unread count badge keeps counting it; the 30-day cleanup never removes it (it only deletes is_read=1 rows). Tapping the stale row again re-opens the accept/decline modal for an already-resolved invite, and the action then fails with 'invite no longer active' (404 'No pending invitation').
- **Root cause:** handleNotificationClick deliberately SKIPS markNotificationRead for type==='trip_invite' (notifications.ts:287-290) with the comment 'the accept/decline routes already remove the notification server-side'. But respond_trip_invite (trips.py:962) never deletes the invitee's trip_invite notification — it only flips/deletes the trip_members row and notifies the INVITER. The modal handlers (share.ts:52-83) call respondTripInvite then close(), with no client-side mark-read or removal either (feed.ts:279-285 is a bare POST). So the notification is both un-read-marked on the client AND un-deleted on the server.
- **Repro:** 1. User A (planner) invites User B to a trip. 2. B opens the bell, sees one unread; badge shows 1. 3. B taps the invite, clicks Accept; trip is joined. 4. B reopens the bell: the 'A invited you...' row is still present and still styled unread; badge still shows 1. 5. B taps it again → accept/decline modal reopens → Accept → error toast (inviteErrorInvalid) because the invite is already accepted. The badge can only be cleared via 'Mark all read'.
- **Suggested fix:** In respond_trip_invite (trips.py), after handling accept/decline, add `DELETE FROM notifications WHERE user_id = ? AND type = 'trip_invite' AND related_id = ?` (invitee, trip_id) so the invite row disappears once acted on. (Alternatively, keep the frontend skip and have the modal call markNotificationRead, but server-side deletion is cleaner and matches the comment's stated contract.)
- **Verifier:** respond_trip_invite (trips.py:960-1067) flips/deletes the invitee's trip_members row and only inserts a notification for the INVITER (trips.py:1061-1065) — it never deletes the invitee's own trip_invite row, and the frontend deliberately skips markNotificationRead for trip_invite (notifications.ts:287-290) while the modal handlers (share.ts:52-83, feed.ts:281-285) do no client-side mark/remove either; the trip_invite DELETEs at trips.py:404 and :1122 only fire on trip-delete / member-removal, not on the normal Accept/Decline path.

### BUG-048 — [P2][bug] Self-leaving a trip sends the leaver a notification saying they removed themselves

_notifications · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:1089-1095`, `src/routes/trips.py:1141-1152`
- **Symptom:** When a non-owner member leaves a trip (self-leave, target == actor), they receive a fresh unread notification reading '{their own name} removed you from {trip}.' — telling the user they kicked themselves, and bumping their own unread badge for an action they performed.
- **Root cause:** remove_trip_member supports self-leave (is_self_leave = actor == target, trips.py:1089) and only uses that flag to skip the planner permission gate. The trip_member_removed notification insert at trips.py:1148-1152 is unconditional and addressed to `target` — which equals the actor on self-leave — with message built from actor_name (the leaver's own name). There is no `if not is_self_leave:` guard around the notification.
- **Repro:** 1. User A owns a trip; invites User B as Relaxer; B accepts. 2. B (or B's client) calls POST /api/trips/members/remove with {trip_id, target_user_id: <B's own id>} to leave. 3. The route deletes B's member row, then INSERTs a trip_member_removed notification to B: 'B removed you from <trip>.' 4. On B's next notification poll the bell shows an unread self-notification.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the trip_member_removed notification insert in `if not is_self_leave:` so leaving a trip doesn't notify the person who left. (The companion-unlink + notification-cleanup sweeps above it are fine to keep.)
- **Verifier:** remove_trip_member sets is_self_leave = (actor == target) at trips.py:1098 but only uses it to skip the planner gate (line 1099); the trip_member_removed INSERT at trips.py:1148-1152 is unconditional, addressed to `target` (= actor on self-leave) with message `f"{actor_name} removed you from {trip_name}."` — no `if not is_self_leave:` guard, so the leaver gets a notification about removing themselves.

### BUG-049 — [P2][correctness] PDF Expenses 'Category' column prints raw category IDs (UUIDs), not names

_pdf · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.92_

- **Files:** `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:684`, `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:688`, `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:1153`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:565`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Personalization.tsx:52`
- **Symptom:** In the opt-in Expenses table, the Category column shows opaque identifiers (e.g. a random id like 'k3f9a2x' from generateId()) instead of the human category name like 'Food'. Every other surface in the app — the budgets PDF section, the in-app budget title, Insights — resolves the id to its name, so the PDF Expenses section is the one place a traveller sees gibberish in the category column.
- **Root cause:** \_expenses_section renders `cat = e.get('category_id') or e.get('category') or tr('exp_uncategorised')` and prints it raw (\_render.py:684,688). Expenses store `categoryId` as the category's `id` (ManualTab.tsx:565 `value={c.id}`), and user-created categories get `id: generateId()` (Personalization.tsx:52) — an opaque UUID, not a slug. The route already builds a category id→name map `_cat_name` for the BUDGET section (**init**.py:1114-1118) but never passes it to `_expenses_section`, and the SELECT for expenses (**init**.py:1153-1158) fetches only `category_id`, not a joined name. The app's own budget-title code (budgets/helpers.ts:226-227) does id-then-name resolution precisely to avoid this; the PDF expenses path skips it.
- **Repro:** 1. Create a trip, add a custom category 'Food' in Settings (gets a UUID id). 2. Add an expense and assign it to 'Food'. 3. Export the trip PDF with the Expenses section toggled on. 4. The Expenses table's Category column shows the UUID, not 'Food'.
- **Suggested fix:** Thread the existing `_cat_name` id→name dict (already built at **init**.py:1114-1118) into `_expenses_section`, and resolve `cat = _cat_name.get(category_id) or category_id` with a case-insensitive name fallback for legacy slug categoryIds (mirroring budgets/helpers.ts:226-227). Translate the 'Uncategorised' fallback (already a key) for empty category_id.

### BUG-050 — [P2][correctness] PDF Settle-up seeds a phantom full-name person for owner-involved settlements, overstating debts vs the in-app screen

_pdf · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.78_

- **Files:** `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:840`, `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:850`, `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:853`, `src/routes/pdf/_render.py:857`, `src/routes/settlements.py:338`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:102`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/balances.ts:107`
- **Symptom:** On a group trip that has a RECORDED settlement involving the trip owner, the PDF Settle-up section shows a phantom extra person under the owner's FULL Google name (e.g. 'Alice Smith') credited with the payment, while the original first-name balance ('Alice') stays un-cleared. The PDF then disagrees with the in-app Settle-up screen, showing more outstanding debt than the app does.
- **Root cause:** Settlements snapshot `from_name`/`to_name` as `users.name` — the FULL display name (settlements.py:338). The roster the PDF builds (and the app uses) keys expenses by the companion's first-name token (the owner is self-stamped under first name). The app's settle math reconciles this via an explicit first-name-token fallback in resolveSettlementParties (balances.ts:107-122). The PDF's `_settle_section` settlement loop (\_render.py:840-861) does plain exact-match: `if frm not in bal: bal[frm] = 0.0; bal[frm] += amt` — so a full-name snapshot that doesn't exact-match the roster SEEDS A NEW phantom entry instead of folding into the existing first-name balance. Expenses balance correctly (they use roster names) but the recorded settlement lands on the phantom, leaving the real debt outstanding.
- **Repro:** 1. Owner Alice ('Alice Smith' on her Google account) creates a group trip with companion Bob. 2. Add an expense Bob paid, split 50/50, so Alice owes Bob. 3. Record a settlement Alice→Bob in the app (snapshot from_name='Alice Smith'). 4. In-app Settle-up shows the debt cleared. 5. Export PDF with Settle up on → it shows a phantom 'Alice Smith is owed' row AND Alice still owing, contradicting the app.
- **Suggested fix:** In `_settle_section`, before seeding a phantom for a settlement party name, apply the same first-name-token fallback the app uses: if the snapshot name isn't in `bal`, try its first whitespace-delimited token against the roster (matching resolveSettlementParties in balances.ts:107-122). Only seed a new entry when neither the full name nor the first token resolves.

### BUG-051 — [P2][correctness] Auto-fill and template pin a bogus 1:1 FX (1 unit = 1 EUR) for no-live-rate currencies (ARS/EGP/VND/TRY…)

_rates-editor · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/utils/manualRates.ts:191`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:210-216`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:413-423`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/currency.ts:71-78`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/presentValue.ts:167-172`
- **Symptom:** For a currency that has no live (Frankfurter) or static rate — ARS, EGP, VND, TRY, CLP, COP, PEN, etc., all addable as FX rows because they live in CURRENCY_SYMBOLS — the editor shows the current-year placeholder 'auto ≈ 1 EUR', and 'Set automatically from my trips' fills (and Save persists) fx=1 for that currency's current-year cell whenever the user has no expenses in it that year. The downloaded template also pre-fills 1. Once saved, Insights 'Worth today' uses manualFxFor() = 1, treating e.g. 1 ARS = 1 EUR (~1000x overstatement) and bypassing the deliberate no-FX Model-B home-CPI fallback in presentValue.ts.
- **Root cause:** computeAutoRate's FX fallback is `convertFn(1, cur, home)` (manualRates.ts:191) and the placeholder uses `convertCurrency(1, cur, home)` (RatesEditor.tsx:213). convertCurrency silently returns the input unchanged for unknown codes (\_rateFor → `CONVERSION_RATES[upper] || 1`, currency.ts:77), so the result is 1, which passes the `rate > 0` / `Number.isFinite && r>0` guards. Neither the editor, computeAutoRate, nor the placeholder consults hasRate(), unlike presentValue.ts which carefully routes no-rate currencies to Model B. Confirmed via probe: computeAutoRate('fx','ARS',currentYear,[],undefined,'EUR',convertFn)===1 (and also ===1 for 2015).
- **Repro:** 1. Ensure ARS has no live rate (offline, or Frankfurter lacking ARS). 2. Settings → Personalization → Exchange rates → '+ add currency' → ARS. 3. The 2026 cell placeholder reads 'auto ≈ 1 EUR'. 4. Click 'Set automatically from my trips' → 'Filled 1 value' with ARS/2026 = 1. 5. Save. 6. Add an ARS expense and open Insights 'Worth today' → the ARS expense is valued as if 1 ARS = 1 EUR.
- **Suggested fix:** Gate the FX live-rate fallback on hasRate(): in computeAutoRate return null when mode==='fx' and !hasRate(cur) and there are no expenses to derive an implied rate; in RatesEditor.autoHint return null for FX when !hasRate(cur); and skip the auto-fill of no-rate FX cells the same way past years are skipped. Inject hasRate into computeAutoRate (it already takes convertFn) or pass a small `hasRate` callback.
- **Verifier:** computeAutoRate's no-expense fallback is convertFn(1,cur,home) (manualRates.ts:191) and convertCurrency→_rateFor returns CONVERSION_RATES[upper]||1 (currency.ts:77) — ARS/EGP/VND/TRY are confirmed absent from the 17-entry CONVERSION_RATES (constants.ts:104-121), so the result is 1, passes the rate>0 guard, and neither computeAutoRate nor the editor's autoHint/placeholder consults hasRate() the way presentValue.ts:240 does to route these to Model B, so a pinned 1 wrongly forces them into Model A; display-only and requires auto-fill/template round-trip.

### BUG-052 — [P2][correctness] Download template bakes auto values as if user-entered — incl. past-year FX = today's rate — so a round-trip silently freezes wrong overrides

_rates-editor · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:441-468`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:413-419`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/manualRates.ts:191`
- **Symptom:** The template is presented as 'the exact shape to edit in Excel and re-upload', but every cell is pre-filled with the AUTO value (currentValueForTemplate falls back to computeAutoRate). For FX, past-year cells with no expenses are pre-filled with TODAY'S live rate. A user who downloads, tweaks one cell, and re-uploads unchanged ends up pinning ALL cells as manual overrides — including past years stamped with the present-day FX rate (a 2015 USD cell = ~0.86 instead of ~0.92). After Save, those years stop tracking live FX / updated CPI and report wrong historical 'Spent' values.
- **Root cause:** currentValueForTemplate (RatesEditor.tsx:447) calls computeAutoRate for any blank cell with NO per-year guard. The auto-fill button deliberately skips past-year FX cells that have no expenses (RatesEditor.tsx:413-419, the PV4-2 guard: today's rate is a misleading baseline for an old year), but the template path reintroduces exactly that value. On re-import every populated cell is written to draft and Save persists it as a hard override (writeMerged), converting auto cells into permanent pins.
- **Repro:** 1. Have at least one USD expense in 2024 and a 2015 column visible. 2. Settings → Exchange rates → Download template. 3. Open the CSV: the 2015 USD cell holds today's USD rate, not the 2015 rate; previously-auto cells all hold computed numbers. 4. Re-upload the unchanged file → 'Imported N values'. 5. Save. 6. Every cell is now a manual override; Insights 'Spent' for 2015 USD uses today's rate.
- **Suggested fix:** In currentValueForTemplate, only emit ACTUALLY-PINNED values (typed draft or storedValue); leave auto cells blank so the template carries blanks (= automatic) rather than baked-in autos. If a populated example is desired, restrict it to the same cells the auto-fill button would fill (apply the PV4-2 past-FX-without-expenses guard and the hasRate guard).
- **Verifier:** currentValueForTemplate (RatesEditor.tsx:447) calls computeAutoRate for any blank cell with no per-year guard, unlike onAutoFill (RatesEditor.tsx:413-419) which deliberately skips past-year FX cells lacking expenses (PV4-2); applyParsedCells writes every imported value to draft and onSave→writeMerged (line 264-271) persists non-empty finite values as hard fx overrides, so a re-imported template freezes today's-rate baselines onto old years; display-only and needs an explicit template round-trip.

### BUG-053 — [P2][data-loss] Deleting a year column or currency row clears the dirty flag, stranding other unsaved edits (Save disabled, silent loss on navigate)

_rates-editor · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:340-357`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:364-377`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx:822-828`
- **Symptom:** User types a new rate in one cell (Save becomes enabled, 'Unsaved changes' shown), then clicks the '×' to remove an unrelated year column or currency row. The typed-but-unsaved value is still sitting in the draft, but the Save button is now disabled (greyed) and the 'Unsaved changes' hint is gone. The user can't save without re-triggering dirty by editing again; if they switch tabs or navigate away the typed value is silently discarded.
- **Root cause:** removeYear (line 354) and removeCurrency (line 374) unconditionally call setDirty(false) after persisting only the deleted row/column. They don't account for other cells the user has edited in the draft. The Save button is gated on `disabled={!dirty}` (line 827), so clearing dirty disables it while unsaved edits remain in `draft`.
- **Repro:** 1. Settings → Exchange rates. 2. Type 0.9 into USD/2025 (Save enabled, 'Unsaved changes' visible). 3. Click '×' on the 2020 column header (or on a different currency's row). 4. Save is now disabled and the unsaved-hint is gone, but USD/2025 still shows 0.9 in the input. 5. Navigate away → USD/2025 = 0.9 was never persisted.
- **Suggested fix:** Don't reset dirty in removeYear/removeCurrency. The delete persists its own change immediately; leave `dirty` as-is so any other pending edits remain saveable. (Or recompute dirty by comparing the remaining draft to stored values rather than forcing it to false.)
