### DSGN-018 — [P2][a11y] Map search dropdown has no combobox/listbox semantics and no keyboard navigation — unusable for keyboard/screen-reader users

_maps · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/mapSearch.ts:102`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/MapSearchBar.tsx:43`
- **Symptom:** A keyboard-only or screen-reader user can type into the search box but gets no announcement that results appeared, cannot arrow-down through suggestions, and pressing Enter does nothing (no 'select first result'). The input is a plain text field and the results container is a bare <div> of <button>s with no roles. SR users have no idea a suggestion list exists.
- **Root cause:** MapSearchBar.tsx renders a plain <input> (no role=combobox, aria-expanded, aria-controls, aria-autocomplete) and an empty results <div> (no role=listbox). mapSearch.ts renderPredictions emits <button class=map-search-row> rows with no role=option, no aria-selected, no id/aria-activedescendant wiring, and there is no keydown handler anywhere (grep for keydown/ArrowDown/Enter returns nothing). Selection is click-only.
- **Repro:** 1. Tab to the map search input. 2. Type 'paris'. 3. Try ArrowDown to move into the suggestions — nothing happens. 4. Press Enter — nothing happens (no first-result selection). 5. With a screen reader, note no live announcement that N matches are available.
- **Suggested fix:** Add role=combobox + aria-expanded/aria-controls/aria-autocomplete=list to the input; role=listbox to #homeMapSearchResults; role=option + unique ids to each row; wire ArrowUp/ArrowDown/Enter/Escape on the input to move aria-activedescendant and select; announce result count via an aria-live region. At minimum, make Enter select the first/highlighted prediction.
- **Verifier:** MapSearchBar.tsx is a plain <input> + empty results <div> (no role/aria-expanded/controls/autocomplete/listbox), renderPredictions emits <button class=map-search-row> with no role=option/aria-selected/id (mapSearch.ts:120), and grep for keydown/ArrowDown/role=option/combobox/aria-expanded across both files returned nothing — selection is click-only.

### DSGN-019 — [P2][design-ux] Wide data tables (rates matrix, expenses/settlements) require easy-to-miss horizontal scroll on phones

_mobile · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/RatesEditor.tsx`, `frontend/static/css/index.css:.rates-matrix-wrap`
- **Symptom:** On a narrow phone the currency×year rates matrix (and long expense/settlement rows) overflow the viewport; the only way to see right-hand columns is a horizontal swipe inside the wrapper, with no visible affordance that more content exists off-screen.
- **Root cause:** The matrix is laid out at width:max-content inside an overflow-x scroll wrapper, so it scrolls rather than reflowing, but there is no edge-fade / scrollbar / 'scroll for more' cue, and a horizontal drag inside it competes with the page.
- **Repro:** On a ≤400px screen open Settings → rates editor with 3+ currencies and 3+ years; right-hand year columns are off-screen with no indication.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a right-edge gradient fade + a thin persistent scrollbar on the wrap, or a card/stacked layout under ~480px.

### DSGN-020 — [P2][i18n] Notification titles/bodies for settled_up, settled_up_reverted and achievement_unlocked are hardcoded English for all locales

_notifications · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/notifications.ts:116-159`, `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/notifications.ts:182-201`, `src/routes/settlements.py:425-438`, `src/routes/settlements.py:596-606`, `src/achievements.py:815-829`
- **Symptom:** A Spanish/French/Portuguese user sees English notification text for several types: the title 'Settled up' / 'Settlement reverted' / 'Achievement unlocked' (and 'Trip Completed!' for trip_public), the body of settled_up_reverted ('X reverted a settlement of ...'), the achievement body, and the third-party settled_up variant ('X recorded that Y paid you ... — confirm with them.').
- **Root cause:** Notification titles render as `n.title || notificationDefaultTitle(n.type)` (notifications.ts:241). The server always inserts a non-null English title (settlements.py 'Settled up'/'Settlement reverted', achievements.py 'Achievement unlocked'), so notificationDefaultTitle's t() fallback never runs — and it has no case for these types anyway. localizeNotificationMessage (notifications.ts:122-154) has handlers for the common types but NONE for settled_up_reverted or achievement_unlocked, and its settled_up regex only matches the simple '{from} settled {amount} {currency} with you for {trip}.' form, not the recorder-variant body — so those bodies stay English. The i18n-drift test (tests/test_i18n_drift.py) only checks en.ts values against es/fr/pt; it cannot see server-side Python strings that never have t() keys.
- **Repro:** 1. Set UI language to Español/Français/Português. 2. Have a companion record a settlement paying you (settled_up), then revert it (settled_up_reverted); separately earn a badge (achievement_unlocked). 3. Open the bell: the title row reads 'Settled up' / 'Settlement reverted' / 'Achievement unlocked' in English and the reverted/recorder/achievement bodies are English, embedded in an otherwise-Spanish UI.
- **Suggested fix:** Add notifications.titleSettledUp / titleSettlementReverted / titleAchievement (+ msgSettledUpReverted, msgSettledRecorded, and an achievement body key) to en/es/fr/pt; add cases to notificationDefaultTitle and handlers to localizeNotificationMessage; and prefer notificationDefaultTitle(n.type) over the English server title for the known types (or stop sending titles server-side for them).
- **Verifier:** Server always inserts a non-null English title ('Settled up' settlements.py:436, 'Settlement reverted' :603, 'Achievement unlocked' achievements.py:829) so `n.title || notificationDefaultTitle()` (notifications.ts:241) never reaches the t() fallback (which also has no case for these), and localizeNotificationMessage (notifications.ts:122-154) has no handler for settled_up_reverted/achievement_unlocked while its settled_up regex (line 148) won't match the recorder-variant body (settlements.py:427-430); the i18n drift test only scans locale .ts files (LOCALES_DIR) so it can't see these Python strings.

### DSGN-021 — [P2][i18n] Changing language from Settings leaves the page's own chrome in the old language (partial repaint)

_settings · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:224`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:269`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:450`, `frontend/static/js/src/i18n.ts:157`
- **Symptom:** A user on Settings → General → Language switches English→Français. The active checkmark on the language card moves, but the page header ('System Control'), the 'Back to Control Center' button, the General sub-tab strip labels (Pills/Appearance/Language), and—if they were on the menu—all the management-card titles stay in English until they navigate away and back (or reload).
- **Root cause:** setLocale() (i18n.ts:157) writes STATE.preferences.locale + emit('state:changed') but never re-mounts or re-navigates. In Settings.tsx the top-level Settings() component subscribes ONLY to the tab store (useSettingsTabSnapshot), and MenuView()/SubTabStrip() subscribe to no store at all. React only re-renders a component when one of ITS OWN hooks fires, so only the store-subscribed sub-sections (GeneralLanguageSection/GeneralAppearanceSection via useStore) repaint on a locale change; the surrounding chrome that renders t() strings does not. paintI18nBindings (main.ts:178) only repaints legacy [data-i18n-key] DOM nodes, not React text. The Personalization page does NOT have this bug because Personalization() calls useStore at its top, so its whole subtree repaints.
- **Repro:** 1) Log in, open Settings. 2) Tap General → Language. 3) Pick a different language. 4) Observe the language card's check moves, but the page H1, the 'Back to Control Center' button, and the Pills/Appearance/Language sub-tab labels remain in the previous language. 5) Navigate to any other page and back to Settings — now everything is translated.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the top-level Settings() (and MenuView) subscribe to the store so the whole tree repaints on state:changed — e.g. call useStore(s => s.preferences) (or a dedicated locale selector) at the top of Settings(). Alternatively have setLocale trigger a router re-render of the current route after the chunk loads.

### DSGN-022 — [P2][i18n] Sessions and Blocked-users settings panels are entirely hardcoded English (no i18n)

_settings · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.97_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:93`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:123`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:168`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:200`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Blocks.tsx:59`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Blocks.tsx:80`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Blocks.tsx:140`
- **Symptom:** A Portuguese/Spanish/French user who opens Settings → Sessions sees 'Active sessions', 'Devices currently signed in…', 'This device', 'Last active … · Signed in …', 'Sign out'/'Revoke', and the revoke confirm-modal copy all in English. Settings → Blocked users likewise shows 'Blocked users', 'Loading…', 'Unknown user', and the 'Unblock this user?' confirm in English.
- **Root cause:** Both panels were shipped with the translation pass deliberately skipped. Sessions.tsx admits it in a comment (lines 118-120: 'keys for these strings can be added … for now we hard-code English'); \_deviceLabel/\_formatRelativeTime, the confirm messages (lines 93-98), the headings (123-127), the 'This device' chip (168), and the button labels (200) are literals. Blocks.tsx uses only 4 t() calls and otherwise hard-codes its strings. The verified locale tables (en/es/fr/pt) are key-complete (1540 keys each, 0 missing), so these surfaces simply never route through t().
- **Repro:** 1) Set language to Português/Español/Français in Settings → General → Language. 2) Open Settings → Sessions and Settings → Blocked users. 3) Observe English copy throughout both panels.
- **Suggested fix:** Add settings.sessions._ and settings.blocks._ keys to all four locale tables and replace the literals (headings, chips, button labels, relative-time fallback, and the showConfirmModal title/message/confirmText) with t(...) calls, matching the rest of the Settings surface.

### DSGN-023 — [P2][design-ux] No pending-changes indicator exists — offline queued writes (and their silent dedup loss) are completely invisible to the user

_sync-offline · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/outbox.ts:229`, `frontend/static/js/src/outbox.ts:236`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:464`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:473`
- **Symptom:** When offline, saving an expense clears the form (ManualTab.tsx:464 resets the form BEFORE the await) and then shows a red 'Save failed' toast (ManualTab.tsx:474-475), even though the write was actually queued and will replay. The user has no way to see that N writes are pending, and no signal that the outbox dedup is about to drop all-but-one of them. listPending()/pendingCount() are implemented and exported but consumed by zero UI (the outbox comments repeatedly reference a 'pending-changes indicator UI' that doesn't exist).
- **Root cause:** pendingCount/listPending (outbox.ts:229-238) have no consumer anywhere in pages/ or components/. Offline saves go through the optimistic path + outbox, but the only feedback is a misleading 'Save failed' (red) toast because upsertExpense returns {ok:false,status:0} on network failure. Combined with the dedup data-loss bugs, the user gets no warning that their offline work is at risk.
- **Repro:** 1. Go offline. 2. Save an expense. 3. Form clears, red 'Save failed' shows. 4. Nothing anywhere indicates the write is queued; nothing warns when a second offline save overwrites the first in the queue.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a small pending-writes badge (the commented-for indicator) driven by pendingCount(), updated on enqueue/drain. Show a neutral 'Saved offline — will sync' state instead of red 'Save failed' when navigator.onLine===false / status===0, so users trust the offline path. This is also the only user-visible guard against the dedup loss until that's fixed.
- **Verifier:** pendingCount/listPending have no consumer in pages/components; offline failures surface only as a misleading red 'Save failed' toast, so queued work and its dedup loss are invisible.

## P3 (67)

### DSGN-024 — [P3][a11y] LoginWall: button-ready transition is not announced; only the loading/stalled states use aria-live

_a11y · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.60_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/LoginWall.tsx:142`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/LoginWall.tsx:143`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/LoginWall.tsx:78`
- **Symptom:** A screen-reader user on a cold load hears 'Loading sign-in…' (polite live region). When Google's button finally renders, the live region is simply removed with no announcement, so the user isn't told the sign-in control is now available — they may keep waiting or not notice the button appeared.
- **Root cause:** The loading and stalled hints are `aria-live="polite"` (lines 143, 149), but the 'ready' path (status==='ready', line 78) just unmounts the loading region and injects Google's GIS-rendered button into #loginWallBtnContainer; nothing announces the state change. Removing a live region does not produce an announcement. The freshly rendered Google button also receives no focus.
- **Repro:** Throttle network, load the login wall with a screen reader: 'Loading sign-in…' is announced, then silence when the button appears.
- **Suggested fix:** On transition to 'ready', emit a brief polite live-region message (e.g. t key 'Sign in with Google is ready') or move focus to the rendered button container so AT users learn the control is now actionable.

### DSGN-025 — [P3][i18n] HeroMap place InfoWindow action buttons/link are hardcoded English ('Add to to-do list', 'View on Google Maps') — not localized

_a11y · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Symptom:** Non-English users see the map info-popup's primary action button as '📋 Add to to-do list' / '✓ On your to-do list' and the maps link as 'View on Google Maps →' in English, breaking the otherwise localized UI. (Accessible name is therefore also English-only for these controls.)
- **Root cause:** buildInfoWindowHtml() hardcodes the button text on line 288 and the anchor text on line 302 as English string literals instead of using t(). This is the integration seam where a POI/search result is added to the to-do list, so the only label on that action is non-localized.
- **Repro:** Switch app language to Spanish/French, open a POI on the home map, view the InfoWindow — action button + maps link are in English.
- **Suggested fix:** Route these strings through t() with new keys (e.g. home.iwAddTodo / home.iwOnTodo / home.iwViewOnMaps) in all four locale files.

### DSGN-026 — [P3][inconsistency] numDays has no client-side upper bound — request a 31+ day range and the result heading lies ('60-Day Itinerary' but only 30 days render/accept)

_ai · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.82_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:291-294`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:328`, `src/routes/integrations.py:600-604`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/AI.tsx:78`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/ItineraryOutput.tsx:116`
- **Symptom:** If a user picks a date range longer than 30 days, the AI result heading reads e.g. '60-Day {Country} Itinerary' and the loading copy implies 60 days, but the server caps the prompt at 30 days so only ~30 day cards come back and Accept Plan creates only ~30 days. The displayed day count does not match what was generated/saved.
- **Root cause:** Client computes numDays = Math.max(1, Math.round(diff)+1) with NO upper clamp (useAiPlan.ts:291-294) and stores it as activeTrip.aiNumDays (line 328). The heading renders savedNumDays = activeTrip.aiNumDays (AI.tsx:78 → ItineraryOutput.tsx:116, key ai.resultHeading '{numDays}-Day {country} Itinerary'). The server clamps num_days = max(1, min(30, ...)) (integrations.py:602), so the actual itinerary length is capped at 30 while the heading shows the uncapped client value.
- **Repro:** 1) Set a 60-day date range. 2) Generate. 3) Heading says '60-Day … Itinerary' but only ~30 day cards render and Accept creates ~30 days.
- **Suggested fix:** Clamp numDays to the same 30-day ceiling on the client (Math.min(30, …)) before sending and before storing aiNumDays, and/or surface a hint that plans are capped at 30 days. Alternatively derive the heading count from itinerary.length rather than the requested numDays.
- **Verifier:** Client computes numDays with no upper clamp (Math.max(1, round(diff)+1), useAiPlan.ts:291-294) and stores it as activeTrip.aiNumDays (line 328) which the heading renders verbatim ('{numDays}-Day {country} Itinerary', AI.tsx:78→en.ts:1012), while the server caps num_days=max(1,min(30,...)) (integrations.py:602), so a 31+ day range produces a heading that overstates the actual ≤30-day plan.

### DSGN-027 — [P3][i18n] Hardcoded English strings on the AI surface (BYO key status, card aria-labels, 'unverified' chip + tooltip) break i18n for es/fr/pt users

_ai · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts:221-225`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/slots.ts:180`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/slots.ts:209`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/AIUsageCard.tsx:96`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/TodoListPanel.tsx:373-374`
- **Symptom:** Users running the app in Spanish/French/Portuguese still see English on the AI page: the BYO key status line ('✓ Key saved on this device.' and '⚠ Saved, but the format looks off (Gemini keys usually start with "AIza"). Click i for help.'), the 'unverified' chip label and its tooltip ('The Places lookup couldn't resolve this. Worth double-checking…'), and the place-card aria-labels/titles ('Open … on Google Maps', 'AI usage today').
- **Root cause:** These strings are inline literals instead of t() lookups. Notably useAiPlan.ts keyStatus uses t('ai.keyStatusEmpty') for the empty case (line 218) but hardcodes the 'saved' and 'format off' branches (lines 221-225). slots.ts:180/209 build raw HTML with English aria-label/title/chip text; AIUsageCard.tsx:96 and TodoListPanel.tsx:373-374 hardcode aria-label/title.
- **Repro:** 1) Switch app language to Spanish/French/Portuguese. 2) Open /ai, expand 'Use my own key' and paste a key → status line is English. 3) Generate with a Maps key → verified cards expose English aria-labels; unresolved items show the English 'unverified' chip + tooltip.
- **Suggested fix:** Route all these strings through t() with keys added to en/es/fr/pt (ai.keyStatusSaved, ai.keyStatusFormatOff, ai.placeCardOpenAria with a {name} placeholder, ai.unverifiedChip, ai.unverifiedChipTitle, ai.usageBarAria).
- **Verifier:** Verified inline English literals: useAiPlan.ts keyStatus uses t('ai.keyStatusEmpty') for the empty case but hardcodes the 'Key saved' (line 221) and 'format looks off' (223) branches; slots.ts:180 aria-label 'Open … on Google Maps' and slots.ts:209 'unverified' chip + title; AIUsageCard.tsx:96 aria-label 'AI usage today'; TodoListPanel.tsx:373-374 title/aria-label 'Open … on Google Maps' — all untranslated.

### DSGN-028 — [P3][inconsistency] Sessions UI device-label re-parser (and its docstring) assume a raw User-Agent, but the server now stores a pre-summarized label — the regex parse is dead code that survives only by accidental fallback

_auth · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Sessions.tsx:43-63`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/misc.ts:11-21`, `src/auth.py:135-173`, `src/auth.py:192`
- **Symptom:** No user-visible breakage today, but the device-label display logic is misleading and fragile: Sessions.tsx::\_deviceLabel runs UA regexes (/Chrome\/[\d.]+/, /iPhone|iPad/, etc.) against a value that is already a coarse 'Chrome on macOS' summary, so every regex misses and it falls through to `raw.slice(0,60)` — happening to echo the summary. The misc.ts AuthSession comment ('server stores the raw header (capped at 120 chars)') is now false.
- **Root cause:** The server changed (R2 audit, auth.py:135-173) to store a summarized 'Browser on OS' string via \_summarize_ua() in \_create_session (auth.py:192), specifically to avoid leaking the full UA fingerprint. The client (\_deviceLabel) and the misc.ts doc comment were never updated to match — they still treat deviceLabel as a verbatim UA. Because the summary contains no 'Browser/version' token, the parse produces browser='' and os='Unknown' and returns the raw summary, so it only works by coincidence; any future change to the summary format (or a label like 'Opera on Linux' that contains an OS keyword) would render a wrong/garbled label.
- **Repro:** Code inspection: pass 'Chrome on macOS' (what the server stores) through Sessions.tsx::\_deviceLabel — all branch regexes fail, function returns the input unchanged via the slice(0,60) fallback rather than via the intended browser+os formatting path.
- **Suggested fix:** Drop the UA-parsing in \_deviceLabel and render server `deviceLabel` directly (with a localized 'Unknown device' fallback), and fix the stale misc.ts comment to say the server already summarizes the UA. This removes dead code and prevents a future format change from producing wrong labels.
- **Verifier:** The server stores a summarized 'Browser on OS' string via \_summarize_ua() in \_create_session (auth.py:192,135-173) which contains no 'Chrome/123' version token, but \_deviceLabel (Sessions.tsx:50-62) only matches /Browser\/[\d.]+/ patterns so browser='' and it returns raw.slice(0,60) — working only by the fallback — and the docstring (Sessions.tsx:43-46) plus misc.ts still describe it as a raw UA.

### DSGN-029 — [P3][inconsistency] initGoogleLogin() renders the GIS button into a #googleBtnContainer element that does not exist anywhere — dead/misleading boot code

_auth · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/auth.ts:147-172`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/LoginWall.tsx:141`, `frontend/templates/index.html:106`
- **Symptom:** No user-visible impact (the real button is rendered by LoginWall.tsx into #loginWallBtnContainer), but initGoogleLogin's renderButton call targets `document.getElementById('googleBtnContainer')`, which is null on every page — that element is never created in any template or component. The function's button-rendering branch is dead.
- **Root cause:** initGoogleLogin (auth.ts:160-171) polls for the GIS SDK and then does `const container = document.getElementById('googleBtnContainer'); if (container) renderButton(...)`. The only login button container that exists is #loginWallBtnContainer, created by LoginWall.tsx:141. So the container lookup always returns null and the renderButton never runs from this path; initGoogleLogin's only live effect is the early ensureGsiInitialized() callback wiring. The dead branch reads as if a second button mount point exists.
- **Repro:** grep for 'googleBtnContainer' across the repo returns a single hit — the getElementById call in auth.ts; no HTML/TSX ever creates that id. At runtime the lookup is always null.
- **Suggested fix:** Remove the dead container lookup + renderButton block from initGoogleLogin (keep the ensureGsiInitialized() call for early callback wiring), or rename it to the real #loginWallBtnContainer if a boot-time render is actually wanted. Reduces confusion about where the login button mounts.
- **Verifier:** initGoogleLogin does getElementById('googleBtnContainer') (auth.ts:163) but a repo-wide grep of src+templates shows the only login button container is id='loginWallBtnContainer' (LoginWall.tsx:141) with no 'googleBtnContainer' anywhere, so that renderButton branch never runs and initGoogleLogin's only live effect is the ensureGsiInitialized() wiring.

### DSGN-030 — [P3][inconsistency] Overall card 'over-budget' threshold uses strict `>` while individual cards use `>=` — same numbers read "Over budget" on the card but "Near limit" on the Overall

_budgets · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/Budgets.tsx:69-78`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/helpers.ts:200-204`
- **Symptom:** When spend exactly equals the target (e.g. €500 spent on a single €500 budget), the budget's own card shows the red "Over budget" chip, but the Overall card above it shows the orange "Near limit" status and color for the identical figures — a visible self-contradiction on one screen.
- **Root cause:** The per-card `budgetStatus` was tightened (audit B5) to treat hitting the ceiling as over: `if (target > 0 && spent >= target) tier='over'` (helpers.ts:200). The Overall tier was left at strict greater-than: `totalSpent > totalAllocated ? 'over' : overallPct > 80 ? 'near' : 'ok'` (Budgets.tsx:72-76). At exact equality (pct=100) the Overall falls through to the `>80` 'near' branch. The B5 fix didn't propagate to the Overall card.
- **Repro:** 1) Create one budget €500 (Trip X / Food). 2) Add a Food expense on Trip X totaling exactly €500. 3) Card chip = red "Over budget"; Overall card = orange "Near limit" + orange remaining figure.
- **Suggested fix:** Match the card semantics: change Budgets.tsx:72 to `totalSpent >= totalAllocated ? 'over' : …` (with the existing `totalAllocated === 0 ? 'ok'` guard already above it).
- **Verifier:** Budgets.tsx:72 gates Overall over on totalSpent > totalAllocated while helpers.ts:200 gates the per-card on spent >= target, so at exact equality (pct=100) a single budget reads 'Over budget' on its card but the Overall falls through to overallPct>80 -> 'near' (Budgets.tsx:74) — a real but cosmetic edge-equality inconsistency, no data impact.

### DSGN-031 — [P3][perf] Budgets page recomputes spend O(budgets × expenses) three times per render with no memoization

_budgets · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.62_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/Budgets.tsx:60-67,300-301`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/budgets/helpers.ts:93-99,120-132,168-185,196-205`
- **Symptom:** For a user with many expenses and several budgets, the Budgets page does heavy recomputation on every render (any store change re-renders the whole page), causing jank when adding expenses or toggling filters.
- **Root cause:** None of the aggregations are memoized. Per render the component computes `allocatedAcrossBudgets(visibleBudgets)` (O(budgets²) containment), `spentAcrossBudgets(visibleBudgets)` (O(expenses × budgets)), `overBudgetCount` which calls `budgetStatus(b)` (= `spentForBudget`, O(expenses)) for every visible budget (Budgets.tsx:67), and then the card map calls `budgetStatus(b)` AGAIN per card (line 301) — a second full O(budgets × expenses) pass. The component subscribes to `expenses` (line 34), so every expense add/edit re-runs all of it. ~3× O(budgets × expenses) + O(budgets²) per render.
- **Repro:** Seed ~1500 expenses and ~15 budgets; open Budgets and add an expense / click a filter chip; observe the recompute cost (≈ tens of thousands of expense iterations per render).
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap `totalAllocated`, `totalSpent`, and a per-budget `status` map in `useMemo` keyed on `[visibleBudgets, expenses]`, and compute each budget's status once (reuse it for `overBudgetCount` and the card map) instead of calling `budgetStatus` twice per card.
- **Verifier:** No useMemo/useCallback exists (grep empty; only useState imported), so each render runs allocatedAcrossBudgets (O(budgets^2), helpers.ts:174 .some over all budgets) + spentAcrossBudgets (O(expenses\*budgets)) + overBudgetCount calling budgetStatus->spentForBudget per budget (Budgets.tsx:67) + the card map calling budgetStatus AGAIN per card (Budgets.tsx:301), and the component subscribes to expenses (line 34) so every expense add re-runs all of it — a genuine but pure-perf issue that only bites at large budget×expense counts.

### DSGN-032 — [P3][inconsistency] ArchivedCard list/drill-in cards render only coverUrl, never the photo fallback — inconsistent with the album overview and detail hero

_collections · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:494`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/helpers.ts:163`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections/ArchivedTripDetail.tsx:91`
- **Symptom:** In the flat list (Group by: none / active search) and inside an opened album, a trip with photos but no explicitly-set cover shows NO thumbnail at all, while the same trip shows a (gradient or photo) tile in the album overview and a photo hero on its detail page. The cover behavior for one trip differs across three Collections surfaces.
- **Root cause:** ArchivedCard only renders trip.coverUrl (Collections.tsx:494 `{trip.coverUrl && <img .../>}`) with no fallback. The album overview uses tripCover() (helpers.ts:163, which adds the trip.photos / day.photos fallback chain) and the detail hero uses the same chain (ArchivedTripDetail.tsx:91-99). So the card list is the odd one out — it ignores trip.photos entirely.
- **Repro:** 1. Trip with photos, no explicit cover. 2. Collections → Group by: none → the card shows no image. 3. Switch to Group by continent and open the album → the same trip's card still shows no image, but the album-overview stack tile used tripCover().
- **Suggested fix:** Use tripCover(trip) in ArchivedCard for the thumbnail (with a gradient/placeholder when null), matching the album overview and the detail hero, so a trip's cover is consistent everywhere. (Note: this shares the hydration caveat in the album-cover finding — trip.photos must be loaded for the fallback to fire.)

### DSGN-033 — [P3][design-ux] Year-album shelf is not in chronological order under the default 'Recent' sort

_collections · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/helpers.ts:187`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:141`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/state.ts:39`
- **Symptom:** When grouping by year (with the default 'Most recent' sort), the year albums appear in an apparently random order — e.g. 2021, 2024, 2023 — instead of chronological (2024, 2023, 2021) or reverse. A user who chose 'group by year' expects years to read in year order.
- **Root cause:** groupTrips() (helpers.ts:187-207) orders albums by first appearance of each key in the already-sorted trip list. The default sort is 'recent' (state.ts:39), i.e. archivedAt-desc, so year-album order tracks the order in which each year's most-recently-archived trip appears — which is unrelated to the year value. Verified by simulation: trips archived in order across years 2021/2024/2021/2023 produce shelf order [2021, 2024, 2023].
- **Repro:** 1. Archive several trips spanning multiple years in a non-chronological archive order. 2. Collections → Group by: Year (keep default Recent sort). 3. Observe the year tiles are not in chronological order.
- **Suggested fix:** When groupBy === 'year', sort the resulting albums by their numeric year key (desc, ALBUM_OTHER last) regardless of the trip-level sort, so the year shelf always reads chronologically. The trip-level sort can still order trips within each opened year album.

_collections · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.95_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:304`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:321`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:337`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:491`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:549`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:553`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections/ArchivedTripDetail.tsx:244`
- **Symptom:** Spanish/French/Portuguese users see English text in: the Sort select tooltip ('Sort'), the year/destination filter tooltips ('Filter by year' / 'Filter by destination'), the card open aria-label ('Open <name> details'), the public-views chip ('Public-link views' tooltip and the 'view'/'views' suffix), and the Share button's already-shared tooltip/aria ('Already shared — click to unshare' / 'Unshare this trip').
- **Root cause:** These literals are inlined rather than passed through t(). It is also internally inconsistent: the neighbouring Group-by select correctly uses t('collections.groupByLabel') for its title/aria (Collections.tsx:288-289), while the Sort/year/destination selects right next to it are hardcoded.
- **Repro:** 1. Set app language to Spanish/French/Portuguese. 2. Collections → hover the Sort / year / destination dropdowns and the 👁 views chip; open a shared archived trip and look at the Share button tooltip. 3. Observe English strings.

### DSGN-035 — [P3][inconsistency] 'Most days' sort counts the day-0 Trip Hub while the card day count excludes it

_collections · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.75_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/helpers.ts:131`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:480`
- **Symptom:** Sorting by 'Most days' can order two trips that both display the same '· N days' label differently, or rank a trip with fewer planned days above one with more, because the sort silently counts the hidden Trip Hub (day_number=0) row that the displayed count omits.
- **Root cause:** The daysDesc sort uses (a.tripDays?.length || 0) (helpers.ts:131-135), which includes the day-0 Hub anchor. The card's displayed day count uses plannedDays = tripDays.filter(d => dayNumber > 0).length (Collections.tsx:480), explicitly excluding the Hub (per BUG-33). The two counts diverge whenever Hub rows differ (e.g. a duplicate day-0 that hasn't been self-healed yet).
- **Repro:** 1. Two archived trips with the same number of planned days but a differing number of day-0 Hub rows. 2. Collections → Sort: Most days. 3. Observe the ordering doesn't match the visible '· N days' labels.
- **Suggested fix:** Make daysDesc count planned days only: sort by tripDays.filter(d => (d.dayNumber||0) > 0).length, matching plannedDays in ArchivedCard and the archived-detail hero's dayCount.

### DSGN-036 — [P3][inconsistency] Non-owner Planner can invite and kick other members via the API even though the UI presents roster management as owner-only

_companions · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `src/routes/trips.py:856-857`, `src/routes/trips.py:1099-1102`, `frontend/static/js/src/permissions.ts:64-79`
- **Symptom:** The frontend tells users 'Roster is managed by the trip owner' and hides all roster controls from non-owner planners (canManageRoster/canInviteMembers are owner-only). But a non-owner Planner can still call POST /api/trips/invite and POST /api/trips/members/remove directly and succeed — inviting new members or kicking other members (anyone except the owner).
- **Root cause:** Server invite gate is `can_edit_trip` (= planner, trips.py:856) and remove gate is `can_edit_trip` for non-self removals (trips.py:1099), only blocking removal of the owner (trips.py:1101). The frontend permission helpers gate the same actions on `isOwner` (permissions.ts:64-79). The two layers disagree on who controls the roster.
- **Repro:** As a non-owner Planner, POST /api/trips/members/remove with another (non-owner) member's user_id — the member is removed, with no UI in the app exposing this.
- **Suggested fix:** Decide the intended policy and make both layers agree. If roster is truly owner-only, gate the invite + members/remove endpoints on `is_trip_owner` (keeping the self-leave exception in remove). If co-planners are meant to manage the roster, expose the controls to non-owner planners in the UI and update the 'managed by the owner' copy.
- **Verifier:** can_edit_trip returns true for any accepted 'planner' role (helpers.py:205-210), so the invite gate (trips.py:856) and non-self remove gate (trips.py:1099, owner protected at 1101) admit non-owner planners while the frontend gates on isOwner (permissions.ts:64-79) — a genuine layer disagreement, but the actor is an owner-granted trusted planner and the owner is protected, so P3.

### DSGN-037 — [P3][perf] No row-count cap or concurrency control on batch import — a large file fires thousands of parallel POSTs and janks the tab

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.78_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/upload.ts:314-447`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/BatchUpload.tsx:94-98`, `frontend/static/js/src/api/core.ts:201-235`
- **Symptom:** Importing a large spreadsheet (a few thousand rows is realistic for a long multi-person trip's Splitwise/Tricount export) freezes the page for seconds and then floods the (single-process PythonAnywhere) backend with one POST per row simultaneously, causing timeouts, outbox churn, and partially-applied imports.
- **Root cause:** runBatchImport processes parsedRows in a synchronous forEach with no size cap (upload.ts:314), building thousands of Expense objects + mutating STATE + calling addTripCompanion per row, then firing `void upsertExpense(expense)` for every row (line 446). upsertExpense → apiFetch uses raw fetch with no queue/throttle (api/core.ts:201-235), so N rows = N concurrent POSTs launched in one tick. BatchUpload's parse also has no row cap (BatchUpload.tsx:95-97). There is no batching, chunking, or max-rows guard anywhere on this path.
- **Repro:** 1. Generate a 5,000-row valid CSV. 2. Import it. 3. Tab freezes during the synchronous loop; Network panel shows ~5,000 simultaneous POST /api/expenses; many time out / land in the outbox; the imported set is partial until retries drain.
- **Suggested fix:** Cap rows (e.g. reject or paginate files over a few hundred rows with a clear message), and replace the fire-all loop with a bounded-concurrency queue (e.g. process in chunks of ~10 awaited writes) so the backend isn't dogpiled and the main thread stays responsive.
- **Verifier:** Verified: runBatchImport iterates parsedRows in a forEach with no size cap (upload.ts:314) firing `void upsertExpense` per row, apiFetch uses a raw fetch with no queue/throttle (core.ts:201-235), and BatchUpload's parse has no cap (BatchUpload.tsx:97) → N rows = N concurrent POSTs; downgraded to P3 because the jank claim is unproven without running and a typical Tricount/Splitwise export is tens-to-low-hundreds of rows (the actual data-loss teeth — server 120/min rate-limit on /api/expenses dropping overflow rows — is already captured by the optimistic-count finding).

### DSGN-038 — [P3][inconsistency] History value-range filter is labeled '(€)' and filters on stored EUR euroValue, but the row's converted line shows the user's (non-EUR) home currency

_expenses · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.66_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/HistoryTab.tsx:255-281`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/helpers.ts:134-137`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/HistoryTab.tsx:300-305`
- **Symptom:** For a user whose home currency isn't EUR (e.g. USD/GBP), the History 'Value range (€)' filter operates on euro amounts while each row's secondary line shows '≈ $X' / '≈ £X' in their home currency. Typing a min/max that matches the visible ≈ amounts filters incorrectly because the comparison is against a different currency's number.
- **Root cause:** applyHistoryFilters compares against e.euroValue (the frozen EUR value) for minVal/maxVal (helpers.ts:134-137), and the filter label is hardcoded '(€)' (HistoryTab.tsx:255). But the row's converted helper line uses formatHome(e.value, e.currency), i.e. the user's home currency via live conversion (HistoryTab.tsx:302-303). So the number the user sees and the number the filter ranges over are in different currencies for any non-EUR home.
- **Repro:** 1. Set home currency to USD. 2. Add a few foreign-currency expenses. 3. Note each row's '≈ $...' line. 4. In History set Value range max to a dollar figure from those lines. 5. Rows are filtered by their EUR value, not the displayed dollars, so the wrong rows show/hide.
- **Suggested fix:** Make the filter currency match the displayed converted amounts: convert euroValue to the home currency for the range comparison (and relabel the field with the home currency symbol), or explicitly state the filter is in EUR and show the EUR estimate on the row to match.
- **Verifier:** Verified: applyHistoryFilters ranges over e.euroValue (helpers.ts:134-137), the label is literal '(€)' (HistoryTab.tsx:255), yet the converted helper line uses formatHome(e.value, e.currency) (HistoryTab.tsx:302-303), so for a non-EUR home the filtered number and the displayed number are in different currencies; minor UI inconsistency (euroValue is the canonical stored value per the money invariant, so filtering on it isn't wrong — only the label/displayed-line pairing mismatches), P3.

### DSGN-039 — [P3][design-ux] Following a blocked user from Friends search shows a false 'Request sent!' success

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `src/routes/friends.py:207`, `src/routes/friends.py:155`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/friends/Friends.tsx:238`
- **Symptom:** If A has blocked B, A can still find B in Friends search and tap the follow button; the UI shows the green 'Request sent!' confirmation, but no follow is actually created. The user is misled into thinking they followed someone when the block silently prevented it.
- **Root cause:** search_friends only excludes users who blocked the CALLER (friends.py:87), not users the caller blocked, so B still appears. `_follow` correctly no-ops on a block edge (friends.py:155-156, returns False), but add_friend ignores the return value and always returns `{status:'success'}` (friends.py:207-209). Friends.tsx:238 then sets searchStatus 'sent' on status==='success'.
- **Repro:** 1) A blocks B. 2) A goes to Friends, searches B's email prefix → B appears. 3) A taps follow → UI shows 'Request sent!'. 4) Reload: B is not in A's following list (the follow was silently dropped).
- **Suggested fix:** Either exclude caller-blocked users from search results too, OR have add_friend/\_follow surface a distinct result when the block gate blocks the action so the frontend can show an honest message (e.g. 'You've blocked this user — unblock to follow').
- **Verifier:** Chain holds end-to-end — search_friends only filters users who blocked the caller (friends.py:87, intentionally per its comment), \_follow no-ops on a block edge returning False (friends.py:155-156), add_friend discards that return and always returns {status:'success'} (friends.py:207-209), and Friends.tsx:238-240 shows 'sent'; but it requires the caller to have blocked the target then re-search them, so the impact is a misleading toast on a narrow self-inflicted edge path → P3.

### DSGN-040 — [P3][i18n] Explore tab is entirely hardcoded English (no i18n)

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.92_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/ExploreSection.tsx:49`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/ExploreCard.tsx:54`
- **Symptom:** Spanish/French/Portuguese users see English strings throughout the Explore tab: 'Finding trips to discover…', 'No public trips yet', 'Be the first — share one of your own…', 'No trips here yet', 'No public trips in this country right now…', 'Show all countries', aria-label 'Filter Explore by country', and on each card 'by {name}' / 'Traveller'.
- **Root cause:** ExploreSection.tsx (lines 49, 61-63, 106, 144-159) and ExploreCard.tsx (line 54) use raw English string literals instead of `t(...)`. The rest of the Feed (Feed.tsx, Friends.tsx) is properly routed through the i18n table, so this tab is an inconsistent gap.
- **Repro:** Switch app language to es/fr/pt, open Feed → Explore. All copy renders in English.
- **Suggested fix:** Extract these strings into the en/es/fr/pt locale files and replace the literals with t() calls.

ExploreCard:54), while sibling Feed.tsx/Friends.tsx have 44/43 t() calls — a real, consistent i18n gap → P3.

### DSGN-041 — [P3][i18n] Feed bundle lines and several event verbs are hardcoded English (i18n gap)

_feed-social · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.88_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/render.ts:186`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/render.ts:326`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/render.ts:333`
- **Symptom:** For non-English users, aggregated Action cards always read in English ('started planning N new trips', 'just completed N trips', 'joined N trips', 'unlocked N new badges', 'settled up N times'), and single achievement/settled-up cards show English fragments ('unlocked', 'a new badge', 'settled up with … on a trip'). Most single eventLine branches ARE translated, making the inconsistency jarring.
- **Root cause:** `bundleLine` (render.ts:186-206) returns entirely hardcoded English template strings with no t() call. In `eventLine`, the achievement_unlocked branch (render.ts:326-332) hardcodes 'unlocked' and 'a new badge', and the settled_up branch (render.ts:333-354) hardcodes 'settled up with', 'on', 'a trip', and the 'someone' fallback. Action buttons' title/aria attrs (render.ts:441,463,472,481) are also hardcoded ('Like','Unlike','Comments','Repost to your friends','Bookmark').
- **Repro:** Switch to es/fr/pt. 1) Trigger ≥2 same-actor-same-day Actions to form a bundle → English bundle line. 2) Unlock a badge or view a settled-up event → English verb fragments.
- **Suggested fix:** Route bundleLine and the achievement/settled_up eventLine branches (plus the action-button title/aria strings) through t() with locale entries in all four files, matching the pattern already used by the other eventLine branches.
- **Verifier:** bundleLine (render.ts:186-206) returns wholly hardcoded English with no t() (unlike eventLine right below it which uses t('feed.\*')), the achievement fallback 'a new badge' (render.ts:329) and settled_up strings 'settled up with'/'on'/'a trip'/'someone' (render.ts:353-354) are literal, and action-button titles 'Bookmark'/'Unlike'/'Comments'/'Repost to your friends' (render.ts:441,463,472,481) are hardcoded → P3 i18n gap.

### DSGN-043 — [P3][design-ux] No map placeholder or error state when Google Maps fails to load — active-trip hero is a blank glass card

_home · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:137-172`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:912-934`, `frontend/static/js/src/googleMapsServices.ts:46-60`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/home.css:474-483`
- **Symptom:** When the Google Maps SDK never loads (no/blocked API key, offline, ad-blocker, corporate network, quota exhausted), the active-trip Home shows a tall translucent/blurred card with just the floating country fact and NO map, NO spinner, and NO explanation. The user can't tell whether it's still loading or permanently broken, and the hero — the centerpiece of the page — looks empty.
- **Root cause:** HeroMap's effect bails when typeof google === 'undefined' || !google.maps and calls whenGoogleMapsReady() (which rejects after a 10s timeout, googleMapsServices.ts:56-57). The rejection path only console.warns (HeroMap.tsx:162-164); nothing renders a placeholder. The #homeHeroMap div stays empty. The card is .cover-card cover-card--md, and .cover-card--md (home.css:483) sets only height + border/radius — no background-color — so the empty map area is just the parent .glass translucent blur. There is a country-select fallback for Maps-unavailable in the trip-create modal (task MK3-1) but the active-trip hero map has no equivalent.
- **Repro:** 1. Run the app with the Maps JS API blocked (block maps.googleapis.com in devtools, or remove the key). 2. Open an active trip's Home. 3. After ~10s the map area remains a blank blurred card with only the overlaid fact — no message, no retry affordance.
- **Suggested fix:** On the whenGoogleMapsReady rejection (and/or when google.maps is unavailable after the timeout), render a placeholder inside the cover-card: a muted background, a small map-pin glyph, and a localized line like 'Map unavailable — check your connection' plus the existing 'Open in Google Maps' link (mapsHref is already computed in HomeHeader) so the user still has a path to the map. Give .cover-card a solid fallback background so a never-initialized map isn't visually empty.
- **Verifier:** Confirmed the failure path only console.warns (HeroMap.tsx:162-164) with no placeholder render and #homeHeroMap stays empty, and .cover-card--md (home.css:483) sets only height with no background; downgraded to P3 because the card still renders the gradient + inspirational quote overlay (HeroMap.tsx:919-924), so it is not literally blank, and it only triggers in the edge case where the Maps SDK never loads.

### DSGN-044 — [P3][design-ux] Fresh-trip greeting re-rolls (text changes) on any background state change because the random pick runs in render

_home · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.75_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HomeHeader.tsx:61-64`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/welcomeCard.ts:73-79`, `frontend/static/js/src/react/store.ts:48-74`
- **Symptom:** On a freshly-created trip (0 days + 0 expenses), the big gradient greeting H1 can visibly change wording while the user is just looking at the page — e.g. it flips from 'Your Italy story begins' to 'Hey traveler!' — whenever an unrelated state update lands (a co-traveler edit arriving via the 15s poll, a theme toggle, an achievement, etc.).
- **Root cause:** HomeHeader calls pickGreeting(activeTrip, isFresh) directly in render (HomeHeader.tsx:64), and pickGreeting picks one of four templates with Math.random() each call (welcomeCard.ts:79). Home subscribes via useActiveTrip → useStore, which re-renders on every state:changed emit (store.ts bumps a version counter and useSyncExternalStore re-renders all subscribers). So any real STATE change re-runs the random pick and the H1 text changes. It only happens while isFresh is true (once a day/expense exists, pickGreeting returns the stable greetingDefault), which bounds the window — but it's a jarring, non-deterministic flicker during onboarding, the exact moment polish matters most.
- **Repro:** 1. Create a new trip (country set, no days/expenses). 2. Stay on Home. 3. Trigger any state change (toggle dark mode, or have a second device/member edit the trip so the poll applies a change). 4. The greeting H1 re-rolls to a different random template.
- **Suggested fix:** Compute the greeting once per trip and memoize it: const greeting = useMemo(() => pickGreeting(activeTrip, isFresh), [activeTrip.id, isFresh]), or seed the random pick deterministically from the trip id so it's stable across re-renders while still varying per trip.
- **Verifier:** Confirmed exactly as cited: pickGreeting is called in render (HomeHeader.tsx:64) and uses Math.random() per call (welcomeCard.ts:79), while useStore re-renders on every STATE_CHANGED via a bumped version counter (store.ts:48-74), so the H1 re-rolls on any state change while isFresh is true; bounded and cosmetic, P3 is right.

### DSGN-045 — [P3][design-ux] No-trip welcome slideshow shows a broken-image glyph (empty alt) when Unsplash is unreachable

_home · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/welcomeCard.ts:36`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/slideshow.ts:228-236`
- **Symptom:** On the empty/no-trip welcome screen, if the Unsplash CDN is blocked or offline, the hero cover-card renders a broken-image icon (with no alt text to fall back to). This is the very first impression for a brand-new user with no trips.
- **Root cause:** The slideshow image element is emitted as `<img id="homeHeroImg" src="${displayImages[0] || ''}" alt="">` (welcomeCard.ts:36) with no onerror fallback, and the 6s rotation just swaps imgEl.src (slideshow.ts:233) with no error handling. Every slideshow image is a hardcoded https://images.unsplash.com/... URL (constants.INSPIRATIONAL_PAIRS). When the fetch fails the browser shows its default broken-image placeholder; the empty alt means there isn't even descriptive text. (The active-trip hero is a map, not an img, so this is specific to the no-trip welcome path.)
- **Repro:** 1. Log in with zero trips (or open the welcome state) with images.unsplash.com blocked. 2. The cover-card shows a broken-image glyph instead of a graceful background.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an onerror handler that swaps to a CSS gradient background (or a bundled local fallback image) and hides the broken img, so the cover-card degrades to a colored panel with the quote still legible. Keep alt empty only if a visible fallback exists; otherwise give it a short descriptive alt.
- **Verifier:** Confirmed welcomeCard.ts:36 emits the img with alt="" and no onerror, the rotation just swaps imgEl.src with no error handling (slideshow.ts:230-235), and every source is a hardcoded images.unsplash.com URL (constants.ts:69-72 INSPIRATIONAL_PAIRS, mapped at slideshow.ts:93); cosmetic and only on Unsplash failure, P3 is right.

### DSGN-046 — [P3][i18n] Localized population-fact templates produce ungrammatical 'thousand' phrasing in ES/PT/FR ('77 mil de personas', '77 mille d'habitants')

_i18n · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/locales/es.ts:158`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/es.ts:159`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/es.ts:161`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/pt.ts:158`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/pt.ts:161`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/fr.ts:163`, `frontend/static/js/src/locales/fr.ts:166`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/place-names.ts:32`
- **Symptom:** For any country/state whose population is in the thousands (Andorra, Bahamas, Alaska, etc.), the localized fact reads ungrammatically: ES 'una población de unos 77 mil de personas' (should be '…77 mil personas'), PT 'cerca de 77 mil de pessoas' (should be '…77 mil pessoas'), FR 'environ 77 mille d'habitants' (should be '…77 mille habitants'). The 'de'/'d'' particle only belongs with 'millones/milhões/millions', not with 'mil/mille'.
- **Root cause:** localizeFact() (place-names.ts:30-41) re-formats the parsed fact through a SINGLE template (facts.country/facts.state) that hardcodes the partitive particle ('de {unit} de personas' / '{unit} d'habitants') which is grammatically correct only for the 'million' unit. The 'thousand' unit (facts.unitThousand = 'mil'/'mil'/'mille') does not take the particle in these languages, so the fixed template is wrong for every thousand-scale country.
- **Repro:** 1. Set language to es/pt/fr. 2. Open a trip whose country has a population in the thousands (e.g. Andorra, Bahamas) — or any US-state trip with a thousands population. 3. Watch the hero slideshow fact: it reads '…77 mil de personas' / '…77 mille d'habitants'.
- **Suggested fix:** Split the template into thousand vs million variants and pick by unit in localizeFact (e.g. facts.countryMillion/facts.countryThousand), or fold the particle into the unit strings (unitMillion='millones de', unitThousand='mil') and drop the standalone 'de'/'d'' from the templates.

### DSGN-047 — [P3][i18n] Home-hero inspirational travel quotes are hardcoded English for the no-trip slideshow (all locales)

_i18n · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/constants.ts:70`, `frontend/static/js/src/constants.ts:85`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home/slideshow.ts:94`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/place-names.ts:294`
- **Symptom:** A logged-in ES/FR/PT user who has no active trip (and any TRAVEL_DATA_DEFAULT fallback path) sees the rotating hero captions in English: 'The world is a book, and those who do not travel read only one page.', 'Every sunrise is a new beginning.', etc. — 12 INSPIRATIONAL_PAIRS quotes + the default quote.
- **Root cause:** In the no-trip branch, slideshow.ts:94 sets `quotes = INSPIRATIONAL_PAIRS.map(p => p.q)` and renders them verbatim — there is no localization path for `.q` (unlike the active-trip path, which runs facts through localizeFact). The quotes live as English literals in constants.ts:69-82 / TRAVEL_DATA_DEFAULT (constants.ts:85). The active-trip path intentionally ignores `.q` (slideshow.ts:162-168), so only the no-trip path leaks.
- **Repro:** 1. Switch language to fr/es/pt. 2. Have no active trip selected (new account, or all trips completed). 3. View the Home hero — the rotating captions are English travel quotes.
- **Suggested fix:** Move the inspirational quotes into the locale tables (e.g. a quotes.\* group as an array) and have the no-trip slideshow pull localized strings; or at minimum localize TRAVEL_DATA_DEFAULT.q.

### DSGN-048 — [P3][i18n] Systematic hardcoded English in React title/aria-label/alt attributes across ~15 components

_i18n · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.93_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:304`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:321`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:337`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/collections-mount/Collections.tsx:549`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/HistoryTab.tsx:329`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/HistoryTab.tsx:376`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/HistoryTab.tsx:398`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/expenses/ManualTab.tsx:840`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/EventCard.tsx:123`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/EventCard.tsx:216`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/EventCard.tsx:223`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/CommentThread.tsx:128`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/BundleCard.tsx:133`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/Feed.tsx:650`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/feed/ExploreSection.tsx:106`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/Profile.tsx:586`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/Profile.tsx:995`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/profile/Profile.tsx:1025`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Settings.tsx:453`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settings/Personalization.tsx:78`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/MapSearchBar.tsx:57`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:957`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:970`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/HeroMap.tsx:1006`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/home-mount/TripBody.tsx:680`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/AIUsageCard.tsx:96`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/TodoListPanel.tsx:373`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/friends/Friends.tsx:433`

- **Root cause:** These components localize their visible text/options via t() but left the title=, aria-label=, and one alt= attribute as English string literals. The repo is otherwise disciplined (no hardcoded placeholder=); these attributes were missed. For sighted users the title= tooltips are visibly English; for screen-reader users the aria-labels are announced in English even after <html lang> is switched, so VoiceOver/NVDA pronounce them with the wrong-language phonemes.

Expenses History: inspect the receipt/edit/delete buttons → English aria-labels. 4. Profile: the home-country / home-currency selects announce English; avatar alt is 'Profile Picture'.
- **Suggested fix:** Add keys for each label and replace the literals with t(). Many already have a visible-text sibling key that can be reused (e.g. common.search, common.delete, common.edit). Change Profile.tsx:586 alt to a t() value (decorative images elsewhere correctly use alt='').

### DSGN-051 — [P3][i18n] a11y skip-link 'Skip to content' is hardcoded English (no data-i18n binding)

_i18n · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.90_

- **Files:** `frontend/templates/index.html:148`
- **Symptom:** Keyboard and screen-reader users on es/fr/pt get the very first focusable element of the app — the skip-to-content link — announced/shown in English ('Skip to content').
- **Root cause:** The skip-link in index.html has no data-i18n-key attribute, so paintI18nBindings (which hydrates [data-i18n-key] nodes) never localizes it. Every other nav label in index.html carries a data-i18n-key; this one was missed.

### DSGN-052 — [P3][i18n] Capital/biggest-city names baked into fact data use non-localized exonyms ('Wien', 'Alger') shown in all locales

_i18n · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/constants.ts:284`, `frontend/static/js/src/constants.ts:293`, `frontend/static/js/src/utils/place-names.ts:41`
- **Symptom:** Because city names are passed through localizeFact() as raw slot values, the fact shows whatever is stored in DESTINATION_DATA regardless of UI language — and some entries use a local/native exonym rather than the user's-language name, e.g. Austria's capital renders as 'Wien' (not Vienna/Viena/Vienne) and Algeria's as 'Alger' (not Algiers/Argel). An English/Spanish/Portuguese user sees the German/French city name.
- **Root cause:** localizeFact (place-names.ts:36-41) only localizes the surrounding template; the {capital}/{biggest} slot values come verbatim from the English source data in constants.ts, which itself contains inconsistent exonyms ('Wien', 'Alger'). There is no per-language city-name table (intentional, to avoid ~960 strings), so the data's own inconsistency leaks to every locale.
- **Repro:** 1. Any locale. 2. Open a trip to Austria (or Algeria). 3. Hero fact shows 'Its capital city is Wien.' / 'Alger.' instead of the expected exonym.
- **Suggested fix:** Out of scope for full city localization, but at minimum normalize the source data to the English exonym (Vienna, Algiers) so the most-common locale is correct; or accept it as a known data-quality limitation.

### DSGN-053 — [P3][inconsistency] Top-spender amount renders bare '0' (no currency symbol) when total display spend is zero

_insights · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/insights/Insights.tsx:1245`
- **Symptom:** In the 'Top spenders' card, the leader's amount shows a bare '0' with no currency symbol/format when totalDisplay is 0 (e.g. every expense's Worth-today valuation floored to 0 by a manual −100% inflation override, or a degenerate all-zero display), whereas every other money figure on the page is formatted as e.g. '€0.00'. Inconsistent presentation.
- **Root cause:** Insights.tsx:1245 ternary `{totalDisplay > 0 ? targetSym + formatNumberForCurrency(topSpenderAmount, targetCurr) : '0'}` emits the literal string '0' instead of the formatted/symboled value in the zero case.
- **Repro:** Create a trip with one USD expense, then in Settings pin USD inflation −100% for that year so todayValue floors to 0, switch Insights to 'Worth today'. The Top-spenders amount shows '0' (no €/$ symbol) while the hero shows the formatted zero.
- **Suggested fix:** Render targetSym + formatNumberForCurrency(topSpenderAmount, targetCurr) unconditionally (it already formats 0 correctly), or apply the same formatting in the else branch.
- **Verifier:** Confirmed at Insights.tsx:1245 — the ternary emits literal '0' in the zero case while every sibling value renders targetSym+formatNumberForCurrency (e.g. lines 1257-1258); purely cosmetic and only triggers when totalDisplay is exactly 0 (a vanishingly rare all-zero-display trip).

### DSGN-055 — [P3][i18n] Overview-map header 'EVERY DAY ON ONE MAP · N PINS' is hardcoded English in every localized PDF export

_journey-media-pdf · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.85_

- **Files:** `src/routes/pdf/__init__.py:504-507`, `src/routes/pdf/_i18n.py:26-263`
- **Symptom:** A French / Spanish / Portuguese user who exports a trip PDF with day maps enabled sees the all-days overview map captioned in English: 'EVERY DAY ON ONE MAP · 5 PINS', while every surrounding section title and label is correctly translated. It is a jarring monolingual island in an otherwise localized document.
- **Root cause:** The overview-pins map header at `__init__.py:505` is an f-string literal `f"EVERY DAY ON ONE MAP   ·   {len(pins)} PIN{'S' if len(pins) != 1 else ''}"` rather than a `tr(...)` lookup. There is no corresponding key in `_STRINGS` in `_i18n.py`. This path is reached on the default export (includeDays + includeDayPins default True) for any trip whose days have coordinates. The PDF-5 i18n pass localized section titles and slot labels but missed this header (and the 'S' pluralization is English-only).
- **Repro:** 1. Set UI language to French. 2. Create a trip with 2+ days that have map coordinates. 3. Export PDF (default options). 4. The overview map above the day cards reads 'EVERY DAY ON ONE MAP · 2 PINS' in English.
- **Suggested fix:** Add an i18n key (e.g. `days_overview_map`) to all four locale tables and render `tr('days_overview_map')` (drop the brittle English pluralization, or store per-locale plural forms). The AI-plan section's hardcoded English ('Gemini-generated plan…', 'BREAKFAST/LUNCH/DINNER/SIGHTS') has the same defect but is NOT reachable from the export modal — modals/pdf.ts never forwards an `aiPlan` — so only this overview header is user-visible.

### DSGN-056 — [P3][inconsistency] History day-total and 'settled' badge use divergent EUR fallbacks for a non-EUR settlement with no euroValue (raw foreign amount vs €0)

_journey-money · verdict: **confirmed** · confidence 0.70_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/viewData.ts:20-24`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/viewData.ts:62-79`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/viewData.ts:169-181`, `frontend/static/js/src/pages/settlement/SettlementView.tsx:397`
- **Symptom:** For a non-EUR settlement row that lacks a euroValue (legacy data, or a future euroValue-less write), the Settlement trip-picker chip / History badge total and the History tab's per-day total disagree: the badge counts it as €0 while the History day-row adds its raw foreign amount as if it were EUR (e.g. 10000 ARS shown as €10,000 in the day total but €0 in the chip).
- **Root cause:** settledStatsForTrip uses settlementEurForTotal (viewData.ts:20-24), which deliberately returns 0 for a non-EUR row with falsy euroValue. But collectSettlementHistory builds each HistoryItem.euroValue as `s.euroValue || s.amount || 0` (viewData.ts:174) — the exact unsafe fallback settlementEurForTotal was written to avoid — and SettlementView's HistoryTab sums those (`totalForDay = items.reduce((s,x)=>s+(x.euroValue||0),0)`, SettlementView.tsx:397). The two surfaces therefore compute the same row's EUR contribution two different ways.
- **Repro:** Hard to hit via the UI today (server stamps euroValue on all new rows), but reproducible with a legacy/imported non-EUR settlement row whose euroValue is null: the chip badge and the History day total for that trip will differ.
- **Suggested fix:** Make collectSettlementHistory use the same settlementEurForTotal(s) helper as settledStatsForTrip for the History item's euroValue (or only fall back to s.amount when s.currency is EUR), so both surfaces agree.
- **Verifier:** settledStatsForTrip sums via settlementEurForTotal, which returns 0 for a non-EUR row with falsy euroValue (viewData.ts:20-24,75), whereas collectSettlementHistory builds euroValue = s.euroValue || s.amount || 0 (viewData.ts:174) and the History tab sums those into totalForDay (SettlementView.tsx:397) — a genuine two-way divergence, but P3 (not higher) because it is latent: the server always derives/overrides a real euroValue on every settlement, so a falsy-euroValue non-EUR row can't be produced through the current UI.

### DSGN-057 — [P3][inconsistency] New-user first-session chain: the biggest landmines are already filed as confirmed P0/P1 in their owning dimensions

_journey-new-user · verdict: **unverified** · confidence 0.80_

- **Files:** `frontend/static/js/src/pages/ai/useAiPlan.ts`, `frontend/static/js/src/bootstrap/auth.ts`, `src/routes/templates.py`

No NEW standalone new-user-only integration defect surfaced beyond those.
- **Root cause:** The new-user journey is a composition of already-audited surfaces; its risks concentrate at the AI-accept and first-login seams, both already captured.
- **Repro:** N/A — see the referenced findings.
- **Suggested fix:** Fix the referenced P0s first; they all fire within a new user's first session and are the highest-leverage onboarding protections.
